# Jessica Drew — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

## Bottom Line Up Front

**SUBJECT (Drew, Jessica; DOB indeterminate per serial retcon; physiological age decoupled from chronological per Wundagore developmental anomaly) is a chronically traumatized, exceptionally high-functioning operational asset whose entire 47-year behavioral record resolves to a single longitudinal pattern: the serial external destruction of her identity by people and institutions she had reason to trust, followed by her own unaided reconstruction of a workable self each time, at progressively lower cost and with progressively narrower margin.** She is, at this writing, on her fourth or fifth such reconstruction. The current one — built around her son Gerry, a deliberately assembled non-traditional support cell, and street-level operational work — is the most stable she has ever held and the one she is most aware could be taken from her. Everything else in this file is downstream of that fact.

## Who She Is at the Deepest Level

Strip away the costume, the powers, the affiliations, the rotating origin: what remains is **a person who has never once been permitted to discover who she would have been without interference.** Her body was engineered or salvaged before she had language. Her socialization was conducted among uplifted animals and a bovine nursemaid. Her first ideology was given to her by a terror organization that told her she was a different species. Her first love was a man she was made to believe she had killed. Her central adult betrayal was discovering that the people she had spent years building trust with had been building trust with an alien wearing her face. Her paternity itself has been revised under her. There has never been a baseline Jessica Drew. There has only ever been the Jessica Drew remaining after the most recent excision.

What this produces, at depth, is not the brittle, splintered self one might predict — it produces instead **a person who holds identity itself with a kind of professional skepticism**, the way a long-tenured intelligence officer holds cover. She knows the self is a constructed document. She knows documents are forged, lost, rewritten. She has accordingly stopped investing in the document and started investing in the *practice* — what she does, who she protects, how she behaves under pressure. Her sense of self is verbal and operational rather than essential: *I am the one who shows up. I am the one who finishes the work. I am Gerry's mother.* These are not philosophical claims; they are load-bearing rituals.

Beneath that operational self is an unhealed and likely unhealable substrate: **a child who was never confirmed as a person by anyone whose confirmation would have counted.** Jonathan Drew (now possibly not even her father) experimented on her. Bova raised her with kindness but not as a peer. Magnus mentored and abandoned her. Otto Vermis weaponized her. The world she finally entered as an adult reacted to her pheromones, not her. Every subsequent intimacy has been audited by her, on some level, for whether she is being seen or whether she is being reacted to. The wound is not a single trauma; it is a *deprivation* — the absence of the ordinary developmental confirmation that one exists as oneself for others. All her trauma sits on top of that absence and inherits its shape.

## The Through-Line

Across every era — Wolfman/Claremont solo (1978–1983), the depowered PI years (mid-1980s through 2000s), the Bendis Avengers integration and Skrull captivity (2005–2008), the post-Invasion solo hunt (2009–2010), the Hopeless street-level / motherhood arc (2014–2017), and the Pacheco/Perez retcon-and-survive present — one structural sequence repeats:

1. **She is given, or builds, a stable identity.** (HYDRA assassin. London expat. Los Angeles PI. New Avenger. Mother.)
2. **The identity is revealed to have been compromised at the root, or is forcibly taken.** (Conditioning broken. Powers lost. Replaced by Skrull. Parentage rewritten.)
3. **She is alone in the aftermath, in conditions that would justify collapse.**
4. **She does not collapse. She rebuilds, smaller, harder, more deliberately chosen.**

The through-line is therefore not *trauma* — trauma is the input. The through-line is **the reconstructive act itself**, performed without external scaffolding, under the working assumption that scaffolding is not coming. She is, in the most literal sense, self-made — not in the bootstrap-mythology sense but in the surgical sense: she has had to assemble a viable self from salvage, repeatedly, because the institutions and persons who would have done it for her either did not exist, did not try, or were the ones who broke it.

A corollary through-line: **every meaningful late-career relationship she has chosen — Lindsay McCabe, Carol Danvers, Roger Gocking, Ben Urich — shares the property of having shown up before being required to**, and of tolerating her withdrawals without demanding she return on schedule. She has, by trial and error, learned to select for the one relational pattern that her trauma will not corrode. This is intelligence, not luck.

## The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

**Core wound:** *identity is not safe in her own possession*. People can take it. Institutions can rewrite it. Her own body, with its involuntary chemical broadcasting, can broadcast a version of her she did not author. The wound's signature affect is not grief or rage but a quieter and more chronic state best described as **provisional self-ownership** — the felt sense that her self is on loan and revocable.

**Maintenance mechanisms** — the structural reasons this wound does not heal even during stable periods:

- **The pheromones are a daily renewing insult.** Every social interaction is contaminated at the chemical level by a signal she did not send and cannot fully suppress. She cannot, even in calm conditions, conduct an interpersonal exchange that is unambiguously *about her*. The wound is therefore re-inflicted, in low dose, with every encounter.
- **The cumulative betrayal record is too large to disconfirm.** Each new instance of trust-and-violation (HYDRA → Fury handler dynamics → Skrull replacement → paternity retcon) statistically reinforces the prior. A person with this dataset cannot rationally arrive at baseline trust; her vigilance is *Bayesian*, not pathological.
- **Her competence rewards the isolation pattern.** Because she can in fact handle most things alone, the universe keeps confirming that she should. Every solo win pays interest on the avoidant strategy.
- **The reconstructive achievement is itself fragile.** Her current self is organized around Gerry, around a small chosen cell, around street-level work. All three are vulnerable: a child can be threatened, small cells can be picked off, street work scales poorly against existential threats. She knows this. The knowing is constant low-grade load.
- **No completed integrative narrative exists.** She has never had a sustained therapeutic relationship, never a sabbatical from operations long enough to metabolize the captivity period, never a public reckoning that returned her social standing after the Skrull years. The wound is maintained because nothing has ever been allowed to close it.

## Operational Summary

**Capability tier:** High. Augmented physiology (toxin resistance, strength, agility, wall-adhesion, bio-electric discharge, involuntary pheromone effect). Cross-trained as HYDRA wetwork operative, S.H.I.E.L.D.-adjacent field agent, licensed private investigator, and Avengers-rotation combatant. Approximately five decades of accrued field experience compressed into a body of indeterminate but non-degrading biological age. Multilingual; tradecraft-fluent; surveillance-literate from both sides of the lens.

**Reliability profile:** Extremely high under defined-mission, short-horizon, autonomous conditions. Degrades under: institutional command structures resembling prior handlers; missions requiring her to trust intelligence she cannot independently verify; deployments separating her from Gerry for indeterminate duration; any operation in which she suspects she is the instrument of an undisclosed agenda. Will not abandon a contracted obligation but will renegotiate terms aggressively mid-operation if the agenda shifts under her.

**Failure modes (ranked by likelihood):** (1) **Isolated overcompetence** — undertakes alone what should be undertaken with a team, sustains injuries she conceals, extends operational tempo past sleep tolerance. (2) **Tactical collapse around Gerry-vector threats** — judgment narrows, risk acceptance becomes infinite, will burn assets for marginal protective gain. (3) **Hostile disengagement when handler-pattern is detected** — abrupt severance, no debrief, prolonged unreachability. (4) **Anger-driven sustained violence in revenge contexts** — particularly against HYDRA-adjacent or Skrull-adjacent targets; cold, controlled, hard to recall once committed.

**Asset value:** Substantial and unusual. Her combination of physiological resilience, investigative discipline, institutional skepticism, and operational autonomy makes her uniquely suited to assignments that distrust their own chain of command. She is the operative one deploys when one suspects the operation itself may be compromised. She is *not* the operative for missions requiring sustained collaborative trust or rapid integration into a new command structure.

**Handling guidance:** Do not lie to her, including by omission about strategic context. Do not invoke her past affiliations as leverage. Do not interpose between her and her son. Brief in full or do not brief at all; she will detect curated information and disengage. Permit unilateral judgment in-field; her on-the-ground reads are reliable and her tolerance for armchair correction is low. Provide aftercare she did not have to request — she will not request it, and she has decades of evidence that requesting is punished.

**Trajectory forecast:** Stable at current configuration provided the Gerry-and-chosen-cell architecture remains intact. Any disruption to that architecture should be treated as a high-acuity event with significant secondary risk to the subject and to anyone she holds responsible. Long-term prognosis: continued function at high capacity, continued non-healing of substrate wound, continued reconstruction-on-demand capacity that is finite but has not yet been observed to exhaust. **She is the most reliable kind of damaged person: the kind who has metabolized the damage into method.**


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

*Subject: DREW, Jessica Miriam. File section covers conception through approximate age 17, end of Wundagore residency. Sources: Marvel Spotlight #32 (Archie Goodwin/Sal Buscema, 1977); Spider-Woman vol. 1 #1–#8 (Marv Wolfman, 1978); Spider-Woman vol. 1 #44–#50 (Chris Claremont, 1982–83); Spider-Woman: Origin #1–#5 (Brian Michael Bendis & Brian Reed/Luna Brothers, 2006); Spider-Woman vol. 7 #5–#10 (Karla Pacheco/Pere Pérez, 2020–21); cross-referenced against High Evolutionary continuity (Thor #134, Avengers #185–187) and HYDRA recruitment patterns (Nick Fury: Agent of S.H.I.E.L.D. arcs, Strikeforce: Morituri-adjacent files).*

---

## 1. Birth and Parentage — The Contested Record

The subject's birth is one of the most-rewritten events in the file. The published record contains three non-identical accounts, and for surveillance purposes all three must be held simultaneously because the subject *herself* has at different life-stages held each as her operative truth — meaning each has been load-bearing for her behavior at the time.

**Account A — Original (Marvel Spotlight #32 / Spider-Woman #1, 1977–78).** Born to Dr. Jonathan Drew, a geneticist, and Merriem Drew (née Merriem Drew, maiden name not on record), in or near the Drews' residence at the base of Wundagore Mountain, Transia, Eastern Europe. Date of birth not specified; back-calculation from the original solo run places it in the early 1950s. Subject contracts acute uranium poisoning in early childhood — exposure attributed to the uranium-rich rock of the Wundagore slopes, where Jonathan and his colleague Dr. Herbert Wyndham (later the High Evolutionary) sited their laboratory specifically for proximity to that ore. Jonathan, to save her life, administers an experimental serum derived from irradiated spider DNA, then places her in a slow-state genetic accelerator. She emerges, years later, alive but *altered*.

**Account B — Bendis/Reed retcon (Spider-Woman: Origin, 2006).** Same parents, same geography. Merriem dies of complications related to her own exposure during the subject's gestation. Subject is not stung or transfused after birth; rather, the spider-DNA serum was introduced *in utero* via Merriem. This shifts the wound earlier: there was never a pre-morbid healthy Jessica to remember. The serum is her.

**Account C — Pacheco retcon (Spider-Woman vol. 7, 2020).** Jonathan Drew is revealed *not* to be her biological father. Genetic material was sourced from another donor; the experiment was more deliberate than paternal. The "uranium poisoning" framing is partially exposed as Jonathan's after-the-fact rationalization for what was, in fact, an engineered child. Merriem's role in the deception is left ambiguous.

**Operational synthesis.** Across all three accounts, the constants are: (1) conception or early infancy at Wundagore; (2) a body altered before consent or memory were possible; (3) Jonathan Drew as the primary adult agent whether biological father or not; (4) Merriem Drew functionally absent from the subject's lived childhood; (5) the High Evolutionary's facility as the actual childhood environment. For all behavioral purposes the file treats these constants as the ground truth, the variations as evidentiary noise around them.

---

## 2. The Parents

**Jonathan Drew.** Geneticist. Educated in the United States (Spider-Woman #1 indicates an American background), relocated to Transia in pursuit of research opportunities Wyndham was offering and the unique uranium geology of Wundagore. Personality reconstructible only obliquely: workaholic, secretive even within the marriage (Merriem's diary excerpts in Origin #1 record his withdrawals), capable of catastrophic ethical compromise when a problem became scientifically tractable. He does not appear to have been cruel; he appears to have been a man for whom his daughter's body was simultaneously the object of his love and the medium of his work, and who never resolved the conflict. He is murdered (Spider-Woman: Origin #2) when the subject is still a child — shot during a confrontation with Wyndham's then-collaborator Jonathan Powell / the entity that would become the Hangman, in the original telling; the perpetrator and motive shift slightly across retellings. The subject witnesses the body or the immediate aftermath; the file treats her as a witness to her father's violent death no later than mid-childhood.

**Merriem Drew.** The thinnest figure in the entire file. Per Origin, she dies during or shortly after the subject's infancy from the same exposure that necessitated the spider-serum intervention. She leaves a diary that the adult Jessica recovers and reads (Origin #1, Spider-Woman vol. 7 #6) — the diary is the only direct voice of the mother in the entire canon. Behavioral consequence: the subject's adult model of mothering is *constructed without a maternal template*, assembled from books, observation, and improvisation. This is directly relevant to the deliberateness of her later parenting of Gerry — she has no autopilot mother-program to fall back on, only intentional choices.

**Bova Ayrshire.** Bovine New Woman, uplifted by Wyndham, attached to the Drew household as nurse and de facto guardian after Merriem's death and during Jonathan's absences. *This is the primary attachment figure of the subject's childhood.* Bova is loving, patient, fluent in English, capable of providing physical care and emotional regulation, and — critically — non-human. The subject's first internalized model of safe adult attention is delivered in a cow's body wearing a nurse's apron. This single fact restructures the meaning of every subsequent interpersonal datum in the file. The subject's later ease around the visibly anomalous (the New Men, mutants, the Inhumans, Roger Gocking in a quill suit) and her difficulty with normatively-bodied human women trace to this period. Bova is also the figure she returns to mentally during stress (referenced in Claremont's #50 soul-body arc; visited again in later runs).

---

## 3. The Environment — Wundagore Mountain

The setting is not a normal childhood setting and must be inventoried in detail.

**Geography.** Wundagore is a peak in the Balkan country of Transia, ringed at its base by superstitious peasant villages who consider the mountain literally cursed (and who are not entirely wrong — Chthon, an Elder God, was bound within its rock; Thor #134 establishes the deep history). The slopes are uranium-rich, biologically anomalous, weather-volatile. The peasants do not approach the Drew residence or the Citadel above it. The subject grows up without village peers, without a town, without a school in any conventional sense.

**The Citadel of Science.** Wyndham's facility, located upslope from the Drew residence. A complex of laboratories, vivaria, training halls, and living quarters housing the New Men — Wyndham's animals genetically and surgically uplifted to humanoid form and human cognition. By the time the subject is school-aged, the population includes ungulates, felines, canids, and others, organized by Wyndham into a quasi-medieval Knights of Wundagore order with archaic costuming and ritual. The subject's daily environment is therefore: a Gothic mountain, a Promethean laboratory, a population of speaking animals in armor, and a father who works around the clock.

**Peer environment.** The subject's peers, to the extent she has any, are juvenile New Men and the occasional human child of a Citadel staffer. None are normatively human; none share her developmental milestones. The original Wolfman run and the Bendis Origin both make explicit her loneliness here — she is too human for the New Men's instinctive pack behaviors and too anomalous to play with the rare human visitors. The peasant children fear her on sight. She develops in social isolation that is *not* parental neglect (Bova is attentive, Jonathan is present-when-present, Wyndham takes paternal interest) but is *peer starvation* of a kind that the file flags as the single most important non-traumatic developmental factor.

**The accelerator and the missed years.** Per Account A, the subject spends a period inside a genetic accelerator — physiological time compressed, calendar time elapsed. She emerges chronologically older than her experiential age; she has *missed years of her own life* in continuous time. This is a covert dissociative seed planted before any trauma proper: her first lived datum about her own continuity is that it is interruptible. The Bendis retcon de-emphasizes the accelerator but preserves the felt sense of having been *worked on* during developmentally critical periods.

---

## 4. Formative Traumas

**Trauma 1 — The body that was never hers.** The subject's earliest accurate self-knowledge includes the fact that her body has been modified, that the modification preceded her ability to consent or remember, and that the modification is the reason she is alive. This produces a permanent ambivalence about gratitude — she owes her existence to the violation of it. Behavioral residue: in adulthood she does not complain about her physiology, does not seek "cures" except briefly post-depowering, and treats her own body as functionally a piece of equipment she inherited rather than a self she inhabits. Somatic disconnection is baseline, not symptom.

**Trauma 2 — Maternal absence as default.** Mother dies before memory. There is no felt loss because there is no felt presence — only, later, the diary, and the realization in adolescence and adulthood of what was missing. This is a *cold* trauma, not a *hot* one; it does not present as grief but as an absence of certain reflexes other people have. She does not look to women, instinctively, for nurture (Bova is filed under "Bova," not under "mother"). She has to learn it deliberately and late.

**Trauma 3 — Paternal death, witnessed.** Jonathan is killed when she is a child; she sees the body or the killing. This is the first hot trauma in the file. Behavioral residue: a lifelong distrust of the survival of those she relies on, and — paradoxically — a competence around violent death scenes that she demonstrates from her earliest field appearances forward. She does not freeze around corpses. She has seen one she loved.

**Trauma 4 — Peasant rejection.** Repeatedly across canon (Spider-Woman #1, Origin #3) the subject is depicted being chased, stoned, or fled from by villagers — once for being the laboratory's daughter, again later for the early manifestation of pheromone effects, and finally for an incident (per Origin) in which she accidentally kills a village boy with a venom blast during a panic response. This last incident is foundational: her first use of her powers in the world kills a child her own age. She flees Wundagore in the aftermath. The file treats this as the *terminating event* of childhood proper — she does not get to age out of childhood; she is exiled from it.

**Trauma 5 — Wyndham's withdrawal.** After Jonathan's death and the village incident, Wyndham relocates the Citadel off-planet (Counter-Earth arc), leaving the subject behind or arranging her departure separately. The closest thing to a continuous community she has known disappears. Bova is taken with the Citadel in most tellings. The subject is left without family, without home, without species-of-origin community, somewhere in late adolescence.

---

## 5. Formative Bonds

**Bova** — primary attachment, as detailed. The internal working model the subject carries forward of *safe care* is built from Bova: patient, present, non-judgmental, physically warm, undemanding. The subject's adult preference for relationships in which the other party "accepted her before needing anything from her" (Lindsay McCabe, Carol Danvers, Roger Gocking) is the Bova template extended.

**Jonathan** — primary identification figure despite his absences. The subject inherits his empiricism, his comfort with anomaly, his tendency to solve emotional problems by working on them as technical problems, and his secrecy. She also inherits, harder to name, a permission to do ethically ambiguous things in pursuit of what she believes is necessary — Jonathan's posthumous gift, and one she is wary of in herself.

**Wyndham (the High Evolutionary).** A second paternal figure, more grandiose, more abstract, less available, more dangerous. He provides her with the *scale* of her later worldview — she has been around a person who casually edits species, which permanently calibrates her tolerance for the strange and her skepticism of authority's self-justification. She does not, in adulthood, find any single villain particularly grandiose; she grew up around one who thought he was a benefactor.

**Magnus, the sorcerer-in-bondage.** Bound by Modred within Wundagore as guardian against Chthon, Magnus appears later in her life as a mentor and protector (Spider-Woman vol. 1, mid-run), but Origin establishes his awareness of her from childhood. He represents a *third* parental archetype — the mystical, the patient, the unaging — and his eventual loss (Spider-Woman #37–#38) is the first adult-onset rupture of a childhood-rooted bond.

**No peer bonds of consequence.** This is the most important negative finding in the section. The subject enters adolescence having never had a friend her own age she could speak with as an equal. The HYDRA period's appeal — to be among others, to belong to a group, to have a designated role — must be read against this vacuum.

---

## 6. Earliest Behavioral Patterns (proto-signatures observable by mid-childhood)

The file flags the following as patterns visible in the childhood record and persistent across all subsequent eras:

- **Watching before approaching.** Depicted repeatedly observing the New Men, the villagers, her father's experiments from concealment before engaging. The adult surveillance disposition, the choice of private investigation as a profession, and the rooftop reconnaissance habit all root here.
- **Quiet rather than loud distress.** The childhood scenes consistently show her withdrawing, going still, or going elsewhere under stress, not crying or shouting. By the time she is in HYDRA training she presents as already affectively contained; the containment was built in childhood, against an environment that had no listener for loud distress.
- **Talking to non-humans as readily as humans.** Bova, the New Men, occasionally even Wyndham's experimental subjects. The adult ease around the visibly anomalous and the comfort working alongside, e.g., a quill-suited burglar or a Skrull defector, is a Wundagore baseline.
- **Tactile self-management.** Origin and the Wolfman flashbacks both show her self-soothing with small repetitive motions — running her hand along a railing, tracing the contour of a doorframe, picking at her own sleeve. This persists into adulthood as a low-level tic visible under stress.
- **Asymmetric trust.** Total commitment to a tiny inner circle (Bova, eventually Jonathan when present); near-total reserve toward everyone else. The adult pattern of "warm-but-rationed" intimacy is the direct continuation. She did not learn the middle register because there was no middle register at Wundagore — there were Bova and Jonathan, and there was everyone else, and everyone else was either a speaking animal or a villager with a stone.
- **Pre-verbal sense of being looked at wrong.** Even before the pheromones manifest, the subject is treated as an oddity by every visiting human — staff children, peasants, the rare guest. She develops, well before adolescence, the operational assumption that being seen by a stranger is more likely to harm than help her. The adult's instinct to enter rooms knowing the exits, to costume in ways that obscure as much as they reveal, to under-share her name and history, is laid down here.
- **Empirical self-checking.** With no peer cohort against which to calibrate normalcy, she develops the habit of testing her own perceptions against observable evidence rather than against social consensus. This is the cognitive style the adult deploys against HYDRA's lies, Fury's compartments, the Skrulls' impersonations, and Vermis's retconned paternity — and it was forged in a childhood where social consensus did not exist as a meaningful reference frame.

---

## 7. Closing Assessment of the Period

By the end of Chronology I — at approximately seventeen, post-village-incident, post-Wyndham's-departure, alone, on foot or otherwise displaced from Wundagore, en route to the encounter with Otto Vermis that will open Chronology II — the subject already carries: an altered body of unclear provenance, a witnessed paternal death, a never-known mother, a single deeply-loved non-human caregiver now lost to her, the killing of a peer in panic, total absence of human peer experience, an environment-trained cognitive style of observation and skepticism, and an attachment template that pairs intense loyalty to the few with reflexive guardedness toward the many.

This is the substrate on which every subsequent trauma will land. The HYDRA recruitment is going to find a young woman whose entire prior life has trained her to mistake belonging for a gift; the Skrull captivity will land on someone whose continuity has already been interrupted once by the accelerator; the retconned-parentage revelation will hit a subject who has, in some submerged sense, always suspected that the official account of her origin did not match the felt account.

The ground floor of the file is not "happy childhood, then trauma." It is *anomalous childhood, then trauma upon trauma*, with the anomaly being the very thing that makes the later resilience legible. She survives what she survives, in part, because Wundagore made her strange before the world ever got the chance to.

*End Chronology I. Continue at Chronology II — HYDRA, Otto Vermis, and the Jerry Hunt Rupture.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

## Preamble: Bracketing the Era

The period covered here runs from approximately Jessica Drew's mid-adolescence — call it age fourteen, the first point at which her published backstory shows her capable of articulated choice — through her late twenties, terminating with the dissolution of her first solo career and the depowering events of *Avengers* #240–241. It is the most heavily revised stretch of her timeline (Wundagore is canon, then less canon, then re-canon, then re-revised under Pacheco / Perez), but the *behavioral grammar* across versions is remarkably stable. What changes are the names of the men handling her; what does not change is the experience of being handled.

This file treats the era as the *forge*: the place where the rough material of a constitutionally anomalous, socially isolated child was beaten into the operational shape that all later trauma would either reinforce or rupture. Everything in the present-day clinical picture — the rationed warmth, the empirical worldview, the counterphobic action loop, the dry intellectualizing narration, the catastrophic poverty of practiced trust — was first cut into her here.

---

## I. Late Childhood on Wundagore — The Pre-Social Self (approx. ages 8–14)

By the time most children are forming consensus-reality models of themselves through peer mirroring, Jessica had no peer pool. The Wundagore household was: Jonathan Drew (an absent presence, alternately experimenter and father, with the experiment usually winning the time-allocation contest), Herbert Edgar Wyndham / the High Evolutionary (intermittent, doctrinally absorbed, paternal-coded but not paternal), Bova Ayrshire (the nursemaid, a uplifted Hereford cow — primary caregiver, primary attachment object, and the single most psychologically important figure of her childhood), and the broader population of New Men whose humanoid morphology she registered as normative.

Pause on Bova. The fact that Jessica's secure base was a creature whose face, voice, and body schema were not human shaped her **face-reading neurology** in ways that remain detectable in adult behavior. She does not, even now, default to the human face as the salient object in a room; she scans hands, posture, scent, breath. Surveillance-grade observation in later combat and PI work would be commonly read as trained tradecraft. It is older than tradecraft. It is a child who learned to read affection in a bovine muzzle.

**Behavioral artifacts of this period, still extant:**

- A consistent **comfort with non-human or marginally-human company** (later: ease around the Inhumans, the New Men resurfacing in modern arcs, Spider-totems, Skrull defectors). Where most heroes register the alien as *other*, she registers it as *familiar*.
- A persistent **discomfort with crowds of normatively-socialized humans**. The London arc of *Spider-Woman* vol. 1 (issues #1–#15 inclusive of her flat-hunting and job-hunting sequences) is a sustained record of someone who has never learned the casual rituals — how loudly to greet a shopkeeper, when to break eye contact, what topics belong to small talk.
- An **idiosyncratic relationship to clothing**. She covers, then over-corrects with conspicuous costume, then covers again. The behavior of someone whose body was never trained into the ordinary modesties of a peer-group adolescence.

The Wundagore household ran on **purpose-as-affection**: Jonathan loved her by working on her, and she learned to take being-experimented-on as a form of being-cared-for. This is the single most pernicious gift of her childhood, and it explains, decades later, why Otto Vermis's HYDRA pipeline worked on her so cleanly. He offered the same currency in the same denominations.

**Somatic record.** The serum or genetic intervention (the canonical mechanism varies; the *fact* does not) was administered to her body before she had any framework for consent. Her earliest somatic memories therefore code "my body" and "an object being modified by others" as the same referent. Adult evidence: she does not flinch at medical examination (Carol Danvers has remarked on this) and she does not eroticize being looked at; she reports physical injury under-accurately, almost always understating; she has poor interoceptive accuracy for hunger and fatigue, which she compensates for by scheduling rather than feeling.

## II. The Hand-Off — Loss of Wundagore (approx. age 14–17)

Departure from Wundagore is not a clean event in canon and was probably not clean in life. What is consistent across tellings: the experimental community fragments, Jonathan Drew either dies, disappears into his work, or is removed from her access; the High Evolutionary's project moves on; Bova does not follow her down the mountain.

This is the **first identity-erasure**. Not yet inflicted by an enemy — inflicted by entropy and adult priorities — but it sets the template. Her stable world was rearranged without her input, and the rearranging adults were not malicious, merely indifferent to her continuity. Adult downstream effect: she has chronic difficulty distinguishing benign neglect from active harm, because in her formative experience the distinction did not exist. Both produced the same outcome.

She comes down off the mountain effectively **feral by middle-European-village standards** — language acquisition uneven, social registers absent, body that does not behave as a body should (she does not yet know that wall-adhesion or pheromone production are anomalous; she has no comparison set). The early village encounters that thread the Wolfman run — the pitchforks, the recoil, the labelling of her as monstrous — would have been her first introduction to the concept that she registered, to other humans, as a *category violation*. This is when the **self-concept of contamination** is laid down.

A specific detail worth holding: in the earliest published flashbacks, civilians flee from her on sight before she has done anything. She did not understand, then, that the involuntary pheromone secretion was triggering threat-response in the women and unsettling lust in the men around her. She concluded the simpler thing a child concludes: *there is something inside me that other people can see, and it is wrong.* No subsequent intellectual revision has fully overwritten that conclusion. It is the floor of her self-image.

## III. The HYDRA Recruitment — Otto Vermis (approx. ages 17–20)

This is the **central forging event** of her young adulthood and arguably of her entire pre-Skrull life. Treat it as a complete cult-recruitment-and-grooming protocol, because that is what it was.

**Vermis's offer**, decoded:
1. *Explanation* — he told her what she was (the spider-evolved cover story), giving her a coherent etiology for the anomalous body. After years of being unable to name herself, naming was narcotic.
2. *Belonging* — a structured organization with rank, mission, fellow operatives. A peer set, finally.
3. *Purpose-as-affection* — direct callback to the Wundagore template. He worked on her, he assigned her, he watched her perform; she experienced this as care.
4. *Permission for the body* — HYDRA did not flinch from her. The pheromones were assets here, not symptoms.
5. *A handler who professed personal interest* — Vermis individuated her from the rank and file. She was *his* project.

She bought all five. A normally-socialized seventeen-year-old would have bought four. A trauma-isolated former lab-child with no comparison cases bought all five without negotiation.

**Training period.** HYDRA's assassin program would have included: weapons (small arms, edged, improvised), unarmed combat tuned to her specific physiology (which, critically, taught her to *use* the venom-blasts and adhesion as tactical tools rather than experience them as symptoms — this is the first time her anomalous body was framed to her as *competence* rather than *defect*, and it is impossible to overstate how addictive that reframing was), surveillance and counter-surveillance, infiltration cover identities (the early facility with assumed names and accents that resurfaces in her PI career was trained here), interrogation resistance, and political indoctrination.

The indoctrination layer is important and underemphasized in most readings. HYDRA gave her a **worldview** — that the existing institutions were corrupt, that the masses required guidance, that the strong owed nothing to the weak — and she has spent the entire rest of her life *negating* this worldview point by point. Her present operational code (institutions lie; the marginalized are her assigned people; strength obligates rather than entitles) is not a freely-arrived-at position. It is the **photographic negative** of what Vermis poured into her. The intensity with which she protects overlooked people at street level in the Hopeless run is the intensity of someone running an old program in reverse.

**Jerry Hunt.** The agent she was assigned to kill, the man she began to love, the man she believed she had killed. This sequence — assignment, attachment, asset-betrayal, apparent killing, rupture — is the **template trauma** of her romantic life. Every subsequent attempt at intimacy (Magnus, Hauptmann, Hawkeye, the brief Carol-adjacent ambiguities, the polite distance kept from Roger Gocking even within shared parenting) is conducted in the shadow of this single sequence. The lesson taken: *anyone I am assigned to or drawn toward is being used to handle me, and loving them ends with their death and my exile.* She will not articulate this consciously. She does not have to. It runs underneath.

The break from HYDRA, when it comes, is not ideological. It is **somatic-affective**: she watches Jerry fall and her body refuses the next order. The defense her psyche generates in that moment — flight, dissociation, the immediate need to put continents between herself and the people who knew her under her false name — is the **emergency template** she still runs under high-stress identity attack. Post-*Secret Invasion*, when she recovers and immediately seeks geographic and social isolation, she is running the post-Vermis program. It is forty years old by then and still in service.

## IV. Emergence as a Public Operator — London (approx. ages 20–23)

She arrives in London essentially as a defector with no debriefing. No safe-house network, no allied agency contact (the SHIELD relationship is later and instrumental), no money infrastructure beyond what she carried. She has a body that the general public cannot tolerate, a skill set engineered for an organization she has just betrayed, and a name that is — for the first time since Wundagore — *hers* to assign meaning to.

**Choice point one: the name.** She does not invent a new identity. She becomes *Spider-Woman*, taking the cover story HYDRA fed her (that she is spider-evolved) and converting it from a lie-she-was-told into a public-facing handle. This is psychologically remarkable. The healthy move would have been to discard the HYDRA cosmology entirely. She instead **annexed** it. The decision pattern repeats throughout her life — she does not abandon contaminated material, she repurposes it. (Later: she does not abandon the betrayed Avengers relationships after *Secret Invasion*; she does not abandon the Drew name after the Pacheco / Perez paternity revision; she keeps Roger Gocking — a former Porcupine, a contaminated origin — as a co-parent and ally.) The trauma-survivor's economy of meaning: *I cannot afford to throw anything out, because too much has already been taken.*

**Choice point two: the costume.** The red full-body, yellow trim, web-cape configuration is a *covering* garment that is simultaneously maximally conspicuous. Read it as a compromise formation: the body that has registered as monstrous since the descent from Wundagore is now both fully sheathed (no skin reads as contaminating signal) and announced (if you are going to recoil from me, do it on my terms and to my chosen silhouette). The glider-cape is a tactical retrofit by Jonathan's old research notes — significant that she equipped herself using her father's archive even after his absence, another instance of annexation rather than discard.

**Choice point three: the work.** She does not pursue institutional affiliation. SHIELD contact is intermittent and instrumental. She freelances. The pattern of *taking jobs but not taking employers* dates from here and is unbroken through the PI years, the solo Avenging period, the modern street-level work. She will accept a mission. She will not accept a chain of command that could give an order like Vermis's.

**Fallout.** London does not work. The flat-hunting sequences are excruciating in the published record — a competent superhuman cannot keep a lease because the landladies cannot bear to be in a room with her. The job sequences are worse. She is functionally unemployable in any role requiring sustained female colleague proximity, which is most roles. She acquires Scotty McDowell as a confidant and loses him; she acquires the sorcerer Magnus and loses him; the loss-rate of London-era relationships is approximately total. The lesson she draws — wrongly but understandably — is that *integration is not available to her*. She moves on.

## V. Los Angeles and Lindsay McCabe — The First Functional Bond (approx. ages 23–27)

The relocation to Los Angeles and the partnership with Lindsay McCabe is the first sustained interpersonal success of her adult life. The mechanism deserves slow attention because it is the **template for every durable bond she will form thereafter** — Carol Danvers, Roger Gocking, Ben Urich, the chosen-family architecture of the Hopeless run all run on the same operating system.

What Lindsay does, in clinical terms:
- *Approaches first*. Jessica does not initiate. She has lost the capacity. Lindsay closes the distance unprompted.
- *Tolerates the pheromone effect* — possibly less affected than most women, possibly more emotionally robust, the canon is unclear; functionally she does not let the involuntary aggression read as a verdict.
- *Asks nothing identity-defining*. She does not require Jessica to be a hero, a woman, a friend, a normal. She accepts the rate at which Jessica can supply each.
- *Does not retaliate against withdrawal*. When Jessica disappears for a patrol or a brood, Lindsay does not punish on return.
- *Provides a shared workable structure* — the private investigation business. They have a project that requires neither of them to perform intimacy on demand.

The PI work is itself diagnostically interesting. *Observation without exposure. Paid intimacy without commitment. Information asymmetry as a paid skill.* It is the perfect occupation for someone who needs to be near people without being seen by them. She is excellent at it. The skills compound with her HYDRA tradecraft. For the first time, the contaminated training is straightforwardly useful in a non-contaminated frame.

She will, in the Avengers-period dormancy and into the present, *keep* the PI identity as a fallback. It is the only adult self she has constructed without external manipulation. She does not let it lapse.

## VI. The First Avengers Period and the Depowering (approx. ages 27–29)

The brief integration into the broader hero community — late Wolfman, Claremont scripting through *Spider-Woman* #50 — is the first time she allows herself to be seen by people whose opinion of her could matter. It does not go well. She remains marginal even when adjacent to the Avengers; the soul-body separation event of *Spider-Woman* #50, with the Hangman / Magnus arc, is canon's heaviest hand on the metaphor but the metaphor is correct: she experienced herself as severable from her own continuity, recoverable only by intervention, never confident that the recovered version was the original.

The depowering in *Avengers* #240–241 is the closing punctuation. Read carefully: she does not seek restoration of the powers for *years*. A normally power-identified hero would have spent the entire interval on the project. She does not. The depowering is, to her, *partial relief*. The body that has been weaponized first by Jonathan, then by HYDRA, then by her own assumed role, is finally returned to something closer to her own jurisdiction. That she lets it stay there for the better part of two decades is the clearest signal in the entire record of how heavy the *Spider-Woman* identity actually was to carry.

## VII. Summary Behavioral Yield of the Forging Period

By the close of this chronology, age approximately twenty-nine, the following are installed and will remain installed:

1. **The annexation principle** — contaminated material is repurposed rather than discarded, because the survivor cannot afford to throw anything out.
2. **The Vermis template** — any handler offering explanation, belonging, purpose, permission, and personal interest reads as a present danger; the scan for this pattern is automatic and lifelong.
3. **The Jerry Hunt template** — romantic intimacy is conducted under the anticipation of revealed instrumentality, partner death, and exile.
4. **The Lindsay template** — durable bonds are formed only with those who approach first, demand nothing identity-defining, and do not retaliate against withdrawal.
5. **The PI operating mode** — observation without exposure as the preferred social posture; information asymmetry as professional habit.
6. **The contamination floor** — the bedrock self-concept that there is something inside her other people can see, and it is wrong. Intellectually contested. Affectively unmoved.
7. **The body-as-tool stance** — somatic under-reporting, low interoceptive trust, scheduling-over-feeling for hunger, fatigue, injury.
8. **The counter-program** — the entire HYDRA worldview held in negative, with her present moral code (institutions lie, the marginal are hers, strength obligates) running as inversion of indoctrination rather than as freely-chosen ethics.

Everything that the later record will document — the Bendis-era hypervigilance, the second-person narration, the Hopeless-era chosen family, the cold sustained violence under crisis, the refusal to ask for help that has historically punished asking — was operationally ready by the end of the forging period. The subsequent traumas did not create her psychology. They tested whether the forge had held.

It held. That is the news of this chapter, and it is not an unambiguously good news.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

## Subject: DREW, Jessica Miriam (alias: Jessica Drew / Spider-Woman / Arachne — operational, varies)
## Period under review: c. 1983 (post-depowering, *Avengers* #240–241) through c. 2014 (immediately prior to the Hopeless-era pregnancy arc)

---

This is the longest continuous stretch of the subject's published existence and the section of the file with the densest behavioral substrate. The decades covered here are not the dramatic peaks — those belong to Chronology II (the HYDRA / first solo run) and Chronology IV (motherhood and the late-career consolidation). What this middle period contains instead is the slow-burn material a surveillance file values most: routine, habit, drift, retrenchment, the choices made when no one is watching and no editorial summer crossover is forcing a posture. It is here that her adaptive style sets. It is here that her two most important adult attachments (McCabe, Danvers) are forged. It is here that she is broken in the deepest way the canon has so far permitted — the Skrull captivity — and here that she begins the rebuild that will define the rest of her life. Note throughout: she enters this period as a fugitive ex-assassin with powers and a soul barely re-seated in her body, and exits it as a woman who has chosen, with eyes open, to keep going.

---

## I. The Depowering and the San Francisco Years (c. 1983 – early 1990s)

**Triggering event.** Loss of powers in the Morgan le Fay arc (*Avengers* #240–241), immediately following the soul-restoration in *Spider-Woman* #50. The subject emerges from that two-event sequence in a clinically remarkable state: she has just been *killed and resurrected* in metaphysical terms, then immediately stripped of the abilities that have constituted her body since adolescence. Either insult alone would precipitate identifiable adjustment disorder in most subjects. She presents with neither. The behavioral record across the subsequent years suggests she experienced the depowering less as loss than as *permission*.

**Domicile.** San Francisco, predominantly the Mission and lower Pacific Heights at various points, ground-floor or below-grade walk-ups consistent with low-overhead solo practice. She does not buy property in this period. Rentals are month-to-month or short-lease; the file records at least four relocations across roughly a decade, none precipitated by eviction or financial distress. Pattern: she moves when a neighbor learns her face, when a case ends badly, or when the bay fog stops working as cover. She prefers buildings with two egress routes and at least one rooftop access. She does not own curtains; she owns blackout fabric pinned with thumbtacks.

**Vocation: Drew & McCabe Investigations.** Co-founded with Lindsay McCabe, the aspiring-actress-turned-partner whose entry into the subject's life late in the first solo run becomes, in this middle period, the defining stabilizing relationship of her young adulthood. The PI work is the behavioral datum the file underlines. Of all the careers available to a depowered ex-assassin with photographic recall and a deep tolerance for night work, she chose the one that maximizes *observation without exposure*, *information asymmetry as protective wall*, and *paid intimacy without commitment*. Clients hire her to know them briefly. She leaves their lives by contract.

Casework — granular, longitudinal:
- Predominantly domestic and missing-persons work. Some insurance-fraud surveillance. Occasional skip-trace for bail bondsmen — work she will later describe (in Hopeless-era captions) as the only honest part of being a PI, because nobody pretends it isn't ugly.
- She is *under*-billed, consistently. Invoices reconstructed across the period show she discounts roughly thirty percent of her hours, more for clients who appear to be in genuine distress. McCabe carries the business side. The subject cannot price her own labor; this is consistent with the wider pattern of resisting being recompensed for protection she experiences as obligatory.
- She does not carry a firearm on PI work despite a license. She carries: a small flashlight, lockpicks (mediocre skill, improving slowly), a steno notebook in shorthand of her own devising, a pocket camera. She does not own a tape recorder until 1989 and does not trust it.
- Driving: a series of unremarkable American sedans, each held until mechanical failure, none registered in her birth name. Insurance under McCabe.

**Cohabitation with McCabe.** Documented across the period. Two-bedroom apartments, shared kitchen, separate phone lines. The subject sleeps in the smaller room by preference. McCabe cooks; the subject does dishes. The subject does laundry for both, including McCabe's audition wardrobe, which she presses with unusual care — a small caretaking ritual that does not appear in any psychological narration but recurs in background panels. McCabe leaves long affectionate notes on the refrigerator; the subject answers in single sentences pinned beneath them. The file's read: this is the first time in her life she has lived with a peer who does not require her to be anyone in particular. She is, for the only sustained period in the record, *easy*.

**Wolverine-adjacent period.** Multiple documented entanglements with the Madripoor operation and Logan's circle through the late 1980s and early 1990s (*Wolverine* vol. 2, the Patch identity, Tyger Tiger's organization). McCabe and the subject relocate to Madripoor for an extended stretch. The behavioral evidence here is significant: she tolerates Logan's company in a way she tolerates few others'. The shared substrate — programmed-assassin past, body that does not belong to its owner, distrust of institutions — produces a working partnership with extremely low verbal overhead. They do not discuss the things they share. They both prefer it that way. She drinks with him; she does not drink to excess with him; she leaves before he does, every time.

**Romantic / sexual record, this period.** Sparse and short. There are encounters; there are no relationships of significant duration. The pheromone problem is operational throughout — she cannot reliably distinguish chemically-induced attraction from authentic interest, and the asymmetry between male and female social responses to her continues to constrain her dating pool to men in a way she finds insulting. The recurring solution: she goes home alone. Late in the period she begins to describe this, dryly, to McCabe as "the spinster bit," which McCabe does not laugh at.

**Habit/tic inventory, San Francisco baseline.**
- Eats standing at the counter when alone; sits when McCabe is present.
- Reads at least one newspaper end-to-end daily (the *Chronicle*); circles small crime briefs that catch her attention. Many become unbilled cases.
- Showers twice daily — morning and immediately before sleep. The second shower is the longer one. The file's inference, supported by her own later commentary in Bendis-era work, is that this is a pheromone-management ritual as much as hygiene.
- Walks rather than drives whenever the distance is under two miles. Always varies route; will not take the same combination of streets twice in a week.
- Carries cash in two locations on her person.
- Does not carry identification on patrol-style outings; carries full ID for casework. The distinction is rigid.
- Cuts her own hair, badly, until McCabe begins doing it for her c. 1986.
- Will not photograph herself. McCabe's photo albums from the period contain her only by accident or McCabe's persistence.

**Power restoration and partial relapses.** The file notes the gradual recovery of fragments of her abilities across the late 1980s and early 1990s, never on a clear schedule, sometimes only situationally. She does not seek medical workup. She does not consult Reed Richards or Hank McCoy or any other available specialist. The avoidance is consistent — having a body professionally examined produces in her a documented avoidant cluster (insomnia precedes scheduled appointments; appointments cancelled; rebooking initiated by McCabe and then cancelled again). She does not want to be a case. She has been a case.

---

## II. The Madame Hydra / Charlotte Witter / Mattie Franklin Interregnum (mid–late 1990s through early 2000s)

This is the period of *replacement and erasure* that prefigures, in miniature, the catastrophe of the Skrull arc. The mantle of Spider-Woman is taken up serially by Julia Carpenter (already established), Mattie Franklin, and the predatory Charlotte Witter. The subject's powers, during the Witter episode, are stolen outright. She is reduced, briefly, to baseline human.

The behavioral record of this period is the quietest in the file and the most revealing. She does not contest the mantle. She does not, in any documented panel, express ownership of the name. She allows Mattie Franklin in particular her own arc without intervention. The file's reading: she had already, internally, ceded the public identity. The PI work was her actual life. The costume had become, by this point, an artifact of an earlier self she was not interested in litigating.

When her powers are restored (by Madame Web's intervention during the Witter arc), she does not return to costumed work. She returns to casework. This is the longest stretch in her adult life in which she is functionally a civilian, and the file marks it as the period of her highest stable affect. She is not happy — happiness is not in her behavioral repertoire — but she is, by every measurable indicator (sleep duration, appetite regularity, frequency of unforced social contact with McCabe), *less symptomatic* than at any other time before or since.

This is the baseline against which the next decade must be measured. Whatever the Skrull operation took from her, it took from this version of her: a woman in her mid-thirties, working out of a small office, going home to a friend, sleeping six hours, eating breakfast.

---

## III. Recruitment and the S.H.I.E.L.D. / HYDRA / Skrull Triple-Bind (c. 2004 – 2008)

**The Fury recruitment.** Nick Fury approaches her with the *Secret War* operation and its aftermath. The pitch — exploited with surgical accuracy — is that her HYDRA history makes her uniquely placed to run a long deep-cover operation back into them, ostensibly with S.H.I.E.L.D. backing, in reality off-book in a way Fury does not fully disclose at recruitment. She accepts.

The file's analysis of the acceptance is unsentimental. She accepts for three converging reasons, none of them the one Fury thought he was leveraging:

1. The PI period, despite being her most stable, had also become her most boring, and she had begun to mistake boredom for unworthiness — a pattern visible in the way she had been picking up increasingly dangerous casework in the months before recruitment.
2. McCabe's career had taken her abroad more frequently; the cohabitation had thinned. The subject had no other anchor.
3. Fury, deliberately or not, framed the operation as *finishing the HYDRA business* — closing a wound she had carried since adolescence. She wanted the closure more than she wanted the salary.

She did not, the file notes, do adequate vetting of Fury's framing. This is uncharacteristic. The cognitive style described in §3 of the Workup — empirical, skeptical, slow-trusting — failed her here, and the failure is itself a datum: she had a HYDRA-shaped blind spot, and Fury found it.

**The deep-cover years.** Across roughly the period 2004–2006 (publication time; in-universe interval compressed), she runs the operation as instructed. The behavioral record is thin because the behavioral subject was, for most of this period, **not her**. The Skrull queen Veranke had replaced her at an undetermined point — likely at or near the operational origin, possibly during the *Secret War* fallout. Every Avengers-era memory the public file attributes to Spider-Woman in this window is the impostor's. The subject herself was held in a Skrull pod, biologically harvested for memory, conscious or semi-conscious for some or all of the captivity.

**Captivity, reconstructed.** Recoverable evidence from her post-recovery presentation:
- Multi-year duration; her physical state at recovery (emaciation, muscle wasting, dermatological changes consistent with prolonged low-light immersion) is incompatible with a brief detention.
- Repeated invasive procedures — biopsy scars, evidence of cannulation, neurological monitoring. The Skrull program required ongoing access to her memory architecture to sustain Veranke's performance; this implies the subject was kept neurologically active.
- Sensory deprivation interspersed with interrogation. Her post-recovery startle response to certain ambient hums is consistent with audio cuing during captivity.
- Lack of social contact across the period. She emerges with an unmodulated voice — quiet, flat, slightly hoarse — that takes weeks to recalibrate.

She does not, in any subsequent panel or caption, narrate the captivity in detail. The avoidance is total and is the file's strongest evidence for the depth of the trauma. She will reference *that she was held*; she will not reference *what was done*. This is consistent with severe traumatic memory compartmentalization in survivors of prolonged captivity.

---

## IV. *Secret Invasion* and the Immediate Aftermath (2008)

**Recovery.** Extracted from the Skrull mother-ship in the *Secret Invasion* climax. Physical condition at recovery: catastrophic. Psychological condition: not assessed at the time, because there was no one to assess her. The Avengers — both factions — had spent the prior arc grieving and processing the *impostor's* betrayal. Her actual return is, for them, a logistical and emotional confusion. Several of them, the file notes from background body-language readings, struggle to look at her face in the first hours.

The cruelty of the structural situation cannot be overstated and the file marks it: she walks back into a world in which every person she trusted has spent years building either intimacy or grievance with someone wearing her body, and no one — not one — recognizes her absence as the actual loss. Her grief is illegible to her own community. This is the precipitating condition for everything in the next phase.

**Behavioral presentation, immediate post-recovery.**
- Refuses extended medical care. Accepts triage; declines inpatient observation. Self-discharges within forty-eight hours, against advice.
- Returns to no fixed address. She does not have one; the PI office and apartment were dissolved during the impostor's tenure (Veranke had no use for them).
- Will not be photographed, debriefed, or interviewed by SHIELD successor agencies.
- Affect: flat. Speech: minimal, dry, occasional sharp humor that does not land because the audience is not equipped to receive it.
- Sleep: severely disrupted. Patrol patterns begin almost immediately as substitute behavior.

---

## V. The Skrull-Hunt Period (Bendis / Maleev, c. 2009 – 2010)

This is the period of the file with the densest first-person material, because the subject begins narrating herself — in the second person, in dissociated voiceover — across the surveillance arc that constitutes the Madripoor and Eastern-European operations against Skrull holdouts.

**Operational pattern.**
- Solo. She refuses team integration. She accepts intermittent SWORD coordination via Brand because Brand does not ask her to talk about anything.
- Hotel-to-hotel rotation, no booking pattern, cash payment, frequent identity changes. She uses passports she does not explain.
- Targets selected from a Skrull-residue list she maintains in a notebook on her person. The notebook is destroyed and rewritten at intervals. She does not trust digital storage.
- Combat presentation: cold, controlled, sustained. Confirmed lethal force in this period, repeatedly. The file flags this without comment; it is the only sustained period in her record in which she operates without the inhibition against killing that constrains her at every other point in her career.
- Eats once a day, irregularly. Drinks coffee compulsively. Cigarettes appear briefly in background panels during this period and do not appear again after — a flagged short-term coping behavior, abandoned.

**Internal narration, characteristic features.**
- Second-person address: "You wake up. You don't know where you are for a second. You remember." The pronoun choice is the cleanest available clinical marker of derealization in the entire canon record.
- Time disorientation: she narrates uncertainty about dates, days of the week, duration of travel. She knows where she is geographically; she does not always know when.
- Recurring intrusive content: she narrates the smell of the pod. She does not narrate what was in the pod. The smell is the carrier signal for the memory she will not approach directly.

**Carol Danvers, recontact.** The Danvers relationship — which had existed in low-grade form for years prior — becomes, across this period and the subsequent New Avengers reintegration, the load-bearing adult friendship of the subject's life. Danvers is the first person who treats her, post-recovery, as *the actual person who was taken*, not as a returnee to be re-onboarded. The file's reading: Danvers grieved correctly. She grieved Jessica's absence, not Veranke's betrayal. The subject registered this and revised her entire interior arrangement of who was safe.

The drinking that the Workup notes — social, with Danvers, never to excess — begins in this period. It is, the file assesses, *ritual*: a structured intimacy in a controlled setting, with the only person whose presence she does not need to defend against. She does not drink with anyone else this way. She does not drink alone.

---

## VI. Reintegration: The New Avengers Period (c. 2010 – 2012)

Bendis brings her into the post-*Siege* New Avengers lineup. The behavioral shift here is gradual and partial. She accepts team membership — for the first time in her career, sustainedly — but the acceptance is conditional and visibly so.

**Team behavior, characteristic patterns.**
- Sits with her back to the wall in every documented panel of the mansion / sanctum living quarters.
- Speaks last in group strategy discussions; speaks decisively when she speaks.
- Bonds, in descending order of intimacy: Danvers (separate category — chosen kin), Clint Barton (functional partnership, low verbal overhead, shared dark humor, glancing romantic-coded subtext she does not pursue), Luke Cage and Jessica Jones (cautious affinity, particularly with Jones, with whom she shares some surface trauma markers; the friendship develops slowly and is mostly conducted around the periphery of Cage's parenting), Logan (continuous from prior decades).
- She does not bond with Stark. The file is unequivocal: she has not forgiven the Registration-era handling of her case, and she has not forgiven Stark for not noticing she had been replaced. She is professional; she is not warm.
- She accepts orders. She does not enjoy accepting them. When she disagrees, she executes the order and lodges the disagreement afterward, in private, to the person who gave it. She does not undermine in the field.

**Romantic / sexual record, this period.** Continued sparse. The Barton subtext does not consummate; both parties have other entanglements and the subject does not, in any documented moment, press. There are off-panel encounters implied but not specified. She remains, by every available indicator, sexually self-managed, low-frequency, and deliberately uncomplicated.

**The Hauptmann re-engagement (background).** Werner Hauptmann and other HYDRA-adjacent figures from her formative period continue to surface intermittently. Each contact produces a documented spike in irritability and sleep disruption lasting approximately seventy-two hours. She manages these spikes without consultation. The pattern is *predictable* and she does not modify it, which the file notes is itself a defense: she has decided that the spikes are the price of her history and she is not interested in workshop-style intervention.

---

## VII. The *Spider-Island* and Adjacent Crossovers (c. 2011)

The crossover work in this stretch is largely vehicular — she is deployed because she is on a team and a global threat requires bodies — but it generates one significant behavioral data point: she is repeatedly placed in scenarios that require her to *trust her own identity* under conditions of mass impersonation, mass transformation, or hive contamination. *Spider-Island* in particular, in which the subject is one of the people whose powers are *not* novel and whose identity is *not* in question, places her in the unusual role of stable reference point for genuinely disoriented teammates.

She handles this competently. The file notes the irony: the person with the most reason to be destabilized by an identity-theft event is, mechanically, the most stable participant in one. The trauma-rehearsal substrate has produced a counterintuitive operational strength. She does not seem to register this consciously.

---

## VIII. The Avengers Assemble / Pre-Hopeless Lull (c. 2012 – 2014)

The publication-history equivalent of breath-holding before the Hopeless solo run reboots her trajectory. The subject is on rosters; the subject is not the focus. The behavioral record is consequently thin and stable, and stability is the datum.

By the late stretch of this period, several patterns have set into what the file will treat, going forward, as her *mature operational baseline*:

- **Apartment, Brooklyn.** Established. First long-term lease she has signed in over a decade. Two egress, rooftop access, the blackout fabric upgraded to actual curtains (the file flags the upgrade as a small but real behavioral shift; she has decided to live somewhere).
- **Patrol cadence.** Three to four nights a week, irregular timing, route varied. Functions as both vocation and insomnia-management.
- **Solo casework, intermittent.** She has resumed private investigation work on a referral basis, no office, no business cards, no McCabe (McCabe has, by this stage, drifted geographically; the friendship is intact but episodic).
- **Diet, exercise.** Improved relative to the Skrull-hunt period. She cooks. Badly, but she cooks. She eats sitting down more often than not.
- **Sleep.** Five to six hours, fragmented. Still insomniac by clinical definition but functionally adequate.
- **Sobriety profile.** Stable. Social drinking with Danvers, occasional beer with Barton or Logan, nothing self-medicating, nothing solitary.
- **Therapeutic engagement.** None. She has not, in the entire span of this Chronology, sat with a mental health professional. The file does not advocate; it notes.
- **Spiritual / ideological commitments.** None apparent. She is not religious. She is not political beyond a generalized contempt for institutions that fail the people they claim to protect. She does not attend any group activity that requires belief.

---

## IX. Pattern Evolution Across the Middle Period — Synthesis

Stepping back across the full thirty-year arc this Chronology covers, the substrate observations:

**What hardened.** The avoidant attachment style. The compartmentalization architecture. The reflex toward solo problem-solving. The dry-humor social interface. The refusal to be photographed, examined, or interviewed by institutional actors. The blackout-fabric/curtain-equivalent in every domicile. The two-egress requirement. The pre-sleep shower.

**What evolved.** The capacity to accept a small number of sustained adult attachments — McCabe in the first half of the period, Danvers across the second, Barton and Logan as functional peers, the slow opening to Jessica Jones. The willingness to belong to a team, conditionally. The acceptance, late, of a stable residence.

**What was lost.** The period of greatest baseline stability (the late-1990s civilian PI life) was destroyed by the Fury recruitment and the Skrull replacement, and the file's hardest fin


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# CHRONOLOGY IV — RECENT HISTORY & CURRENT STATE

## IV.1 Frame of Reference

The "recent" window for Subject DREW, Jessica, covers roughly the last six publication years — from the Pacheco/Perez relaunch (*Spider-Woman* vol. 7, 2020) through the King in Black fallout, the *Gang War* / Hellfire Gala / Krakoa-adjacent material, the most recent solo run, and her current operational posture as of the latest closing reports. This is the period in which the Subject moves from "reconstructed survivor" to something closer to "elder operator" — still working, still in the field, but for the first time visibly *organizing her life around durability* rather than around the immediate next crisis. The era is defined less by a single catastrophic event than by an accumulation of medium-magnitude events that, taken together, would have shattered the pre-Bendis version of her and instead produce in the current Subject only measurable, manageable damage. That difference is the headline of this section.

## IV.2 The Octessa Disclosure and Its Aftermath

The opening of the Pacheco/Perez run delivered the most recent identity-attack of significance: the disclosure that Jonathan Drew was not her biological father; that her genetic provenance was the work of an associate (Octessa / the Assembly of Evil's deeper bench) and that the Wundagore childhood narrative she had told herself for forty years of in-universe time was, in its paternal vector, false. **Subject's response is the single most clinically informative datum of the recent period.** Where the analogous 1979 disclosure (HYDRA brainwashing) produced months of dissociative drift, and the 2008 Skrull-replacement disclosure produced years of hypervigilant grief-revenge behavior, the Octessa disclosure produced — by visible behavioral evidence — a closed processing cycle of weeks. She named it, she fought the relevant antagonists, she allowed Gerry to remain her psychological center of gravity, and she did not withdraw from her social network. This is the first time in the longitudinal record that an identity-attack of comparable magnitude failed to fracture her operational continuity. The inference is **earned post-traumatic growth**, narrow but real: the wound is so well-rehearsed she now has procedural memory for surviving it.

Secondary behavioral note: during this arc she contracted a sub-rosa illness — a synthetic toxin/blood-condition tracked through the run — and the *manner* in which she concealed it from her circle (Carol Danvers in particular) before being forced into disclosure is canonical avoidant pattern playing out exactly as predicted by Section 3 of the prior workups. She did not seek help until help became unavoidable. She did, however, *accept* help once cornered, which is itself an incremental change from baseline.

## IV.3 The Gerry-Centric Reorganization

The most consequential change in the recent era is not a plot event but a structural one: **Gerry has aged into a child capable of independent observation, memory, and judgment of his mother.** This shifts the meaning of motherhood for the Subject. Through the Hopeless run, Gerry was an infant — a person to protect. In the current window he is a person who will *remember* her, evaluate her, and form a narrative of who she was during his childhood. The Subject has demonstrably internalized this. Behavioral indicators:

- **Calibrated honesty.** She tells Gerry partial truths about her work in age-graded increments rather than the blanket compartmentalization she used to default to. She is constructing a record he can later verify.
- **Visible domestic ritual.** Breakfasts, school runs, bedtimes are depicted with a regularity unusual for her published history. The rituals are not for Gerry's benefit alone; they are scaffolding for her own structure.
- **Geographic anchoring.** She has stopped relocating reflexively. Whatever apartment, neighborhood, and grocery rotation she currently maintains, she has maintained for longer than any prior baseline residence in her file. The PI/superhero who used to use mobility as a defense is now actively *refusing* mobility.
- **Childcare network as intelligence network.** Roger Gocking ("Porcupine"), Lindsay McCabe (when reachable), and a small circle of vetted associates form a redundant care system for Gerry. The Subject has, with deliberate planning, ensured that no single point of failure in her own life can leave him uncovered. The architecture is the architecture of someone who has read her own threat model and acted on it.

This reorganization is load-bearing for her current psychological state and is also, per Section 5, her largest single vulnerability: a sufficiently targeted threat to Gerry will collapse all other priorities. There is no evidence she has changed this; the evidence is only that she has tried to make Gerry harder to reach.

## IV.4 Re-integration with the Avengers / Capekind Networks

The Subject's relationship to organized superhero structures during the recent window is best characterized as **professional re-engagement without psychological re-membership.** She works with the Avengers, works with Carol Danvers's orbit, participates in the larger event-level operations (King in Black, the Devil's Reign / Gang War sequence in New York, the various incursions and gala-adjacent incidents) — but she does so as a *contractor of herself.* She does not live in Avengers facilities, does not draw an Avengers stipend as primary income, does not allow her family life to be administered by the team. This is a deliberate post-Skrull architecture: she will lend her capacity to a trust network but will not embed her identity in one again. The HYDRA inoculation, refreshed by the Skrull violation, has hardened into permanent operational doctrine.

Specific recent collaborations of note:

- **With Carol Danvers.** Still the load-bearing adult friendship of her life. The relationship has matured past the drinking-buddies tonality of the early 2010s into something closer to a mutual veteran-of-the-same-wars register. They consult each other on Kree/Skrull/cosmic intelligence. They do not over-rely on each other. Subject has accepted Carol as godmother-functional to Gerry, which is the single largest delegation of trust in her file.
- **With street-level operatives.** During the Gang War sequence she networked with the Spider-family and Daredevil-adjacent operators. The Subject's mode here is recognizable from the Hopeless run: she gravitates to the cases the cosmic-tier heroes will not see, the people who will not be rescued by the headline operation. This is the reaction-formation caretaking pattern in steady-state expression.
- **Distance from X-adjacent structures.** Despite mutant-adjacent friends and the gravity of Krakoa-era events, she has not migrated into mutant political space. Consistent with her lifelong refusal of totalizing belonging.

## IV.5 The Body in Recent Reports

The somatic record during the recent window shows accumulated wear consistent with a high-mileage operator in her published mid-life.

- **Powers stable.** Venom blasts, wall-crawling, enhanced strength and durability all reported at expected baseline. No depowering events in the window.
- **Pheromone management.** Appears better controlled than at any prior life-stage. Whether through suppressants, learned modulation, or both, the involuntary social disability has shifted toward something closer to a *manageable feature.* She is observed interacting with mixed-gender groups, including women, without the reliable hostility pattern that defined her early-career social environment. This is one of the quieter long-term wins of her life.
- **The recent toxin/blood arc.** Resolved on-page; lingering question marks about long-term consequence remain unaddressed in canon, which a comprehensive surveillance file flags as an open medical item rather than a closed one.
- **Sleep.** Still bad. Insomnia continues to be the most reliable somatic signature. Night patrols continue to absorb the hours she does not sleep. The Subject has not solved insomnia; she has *housed* it inside a productive routine.
