She has, on every route, a small number of *anchor stops* — a particular roof, a particular alley, a particular all-night counter — where she pauses without obvious purpose.
- **Eating.** Standing, often. From the refrigerator door. Two real meals a day when domestic, one when operational. Will eat what Gerry eats when supervising him; will eat almost nothing when alone for stretches.
- **Sleep.** Light, broken, configurable. Sleeps on her left side, facing the door, in operational contexts; will sleep on her back, arms at her sides, only in safehouses she trusts absolutely. The bedside is kept clear of clutter — phone, glass of water, no books. The book is on the floor.
- **Phone hygiene.** Multiple devices. Carries two at minimum during operations. The personal phone has a small number of contacts — Lindsay, Carol, Roger, Gerry's school, Ben Urich's old contacts updated forward. The operational phone is replaced on a schedule the file has been unable to determine.
- **Money.** Cash preference for daily life. Maintains accessible funds in at least two jurisdictions. The PI practice provides clean documentable income; the Avengers stipend goes largely unused.
- **Clothing.** Practical, layered, dark-toned in operational contexts; warmer palette in domestic ones. Wears closed-toe shoes essentially always; the file has no record of her in open footwear in any non-vacation context. The classic costume is kept accessible but not displayed.
- **Apartment.** Cold, low-lit, minimal. Few photographs (one of Gerry on a shelf; nothing visible of any romantic partner past or present; one item from Wundagore she has carried through every move). Books in stacks rather than shelves. Sightlines from the kitchen to the front door clear at all times.

---

## VIII. VICTORY

She does not celebrate. She decompresses.

**Somatic.** Releases visible tension only after she is alone or with one trusted person — shoulders drop, jaw unclenches, often a long exhale she has been holding without registering. Sleeps hard after victory, often for ten or twelve hours, which is anomalous for her baseline insomnia and suggests the activation has been holding the sleep deficit in suspension.

**Kinesic.** Half-smile, more often than full. Will accept a hug from Carol; will not accept one from a colleague. Becomes briefly more tactile with Gerry — picks him up more, holds him longer.

**Paralinguistic.** The hoarse low laugh returns. Voice drops back to its private register, sometimes for several hours.

**Linguistic.** Self-deprecation about her own role. Will credit others extensively and accept credit poorly. This is consistent and not modesty performance; she has a documented discomfort with being singled out as having done something well, related to the deeper discomfort with being *seen* as an identifiable agent rather than as a tool or a face.

**Decision habits.** Does not capitalize on victory by taking on additional work. The pattern is closer to *bank the win and rest*. This is unusual in the operational community and is one of the healthier instincts in the file.

---

## IX. DEFEAT

She metabolizes defeat better than victory in some respects — she has more practice.

**Somatic.** No physical performance of defeat. Carriage does not change; gait does not change. The signal is the absence of signal — she becomes harder to read, not easier.

**Kinesic.** The asymmetric weight-bearing returns immediately; the trained even-grounding of threat-state goes off as soon as the situation is concluded. She sits down. She rarely sits down in any other state without reason; sitting after defeat is a recognizable tell.

**Paralinguistic.** Voice goes flat and clean. Sentences become declarative and short. She will state outcomes without softening: *we lost him. she's dead. it didn't work.* No euphemism. This is a discipline she imposes on herself.

**Linguistic.** Refuses post-mortem theater. Will conduct an actual operational debrief in detail and at length — she is rigorous about understanding what failed — but will not engage in collective lamentation. Has been observed to leave rooms where collective lamentation begins.

**Decision habits.** Tendency to over-assign causation to herself. Will identify her own decision-points in the failure chain and weight them heavily; will under-weight others' contributions to the failure. This is a clinical artifact — the C-PTSD negative self-concept doing its work — and it is the cognitive distortion she has the least insight into. She knows about her counterphobic engagement; she knows about her isolation tendency; she has not yet recognized the over-attribution of failure to self.

**Recovery.** Returns to baseline through work, not rest. The opposite pattern from victory. Defeat sends her back into patrol immediately; the wandering route variant appears. Will go without sleep for thirty-six to forty-eight hours after a serious loss, then crash. The crash is total and brief and she returns to function the morning after.

---

## X. IDENTITY-ATTACK CONDITIONS

A separate category, because the attack on her identity is the unique threat-class for this subject and produces a behavioral profile that does not map cleanly onto ordinary threat response.

**Triggers.** Mind control attempts, impersonation, retconned-history reveals, accusations of being a double agent, situations in which her allies cannot tell whether she is herself, any echo of the HYDRA / Skrull / Fury "you were a tool the whole time" pattern.

**Somatic.** Immediate sympathetic activation that does *not* settle the way threat-state activation does. The breathing-slow inhibition is harder to engage. Hands tremble briefly — one of the very few contexts in which her hands tremble. Skin pales rather than flushing.

**Kinesic.** Closes posture for the first beat, then forces open. The forcing is visible. She has rehearsed not flinching from this kind of attack and the rehearsal shows in the slight deliberate quality of the openness.

**Paralinguistic.** Voice drops further than threat-state — close to a whisper at times — and becomes very precise. This is the most controlled vocal register she has, and it appears only here.

**Linguistic.** Will state who she is, factually and minimally, often without prompting. *I'm Jessica. Gerry's mother. I work out of the same office I've worked out of for two years.* The factual self-anchoring is a coping tool developed after *Secret Invasion* and refined post-Pacheco-era parentage revelation.

**Decision habits.** Hostile disengagement from the source of the identity-attack, fast and total. Will not negotiate, will not explain, will exit. If the source is someone she had trusted, the trust is suspended pending evidence, not revoked — she has learned to distinguish — but the suspension is functionally indist


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## Preliminary Note on Method

What follows is reconstructed from the longitudinal behavioral record (1977–present) and extrapolated to the granular texture a sustained surveillance package would actually capture: timestamps, routes, vendors, postures, repetitions. The subject's life splits cleanly into three operational frames — *solo operative period* (pre-Gerry), *single-mother operative period* (post-2015), and *crisis-displacement weeks* (mission-active, child-offloaded). Each has its own clock. The architecture below treats the present, post-2020 single-mother frame as baseline; deviations into the other frames are flagged.

---

## 1. The Architecture of Her Day

### 1.1 Wake

Subject does not use an alarm. She has not used one reliably since the Skrull recovery. She wakes between 0430 and 0530, almost always after less than five hours of contiguous sleep, often after waking once or twice in the night and re-settling without checking the time (deliberate — she has trained herself out of clock-checking because it accelerates the next insomniac spiral). The first action upon waking is auditory triage: she lies still for forty to ninety seconds, eyes open, cataloguing the apartment's sound profile — refrigerator compressor, building HVAC, neighbor footfalls, street, Gerry's breathing if he is home. Only after the audit does she sit up.

Second action: hand to the underside of the bedframe, confirming the holdout (a compact bio-electric capacitor sidearm in the pre-power-restoration arcs; in current canon, a knife and a phone). The check is not anxious. It is liturgical. She does it the way a Catholic crosses themselves at a doorway.

Third action: window. She crosses to it before any other room-business, parts the blind a half-inch, scans the opposing roofline and the street at the two predictable surveillance angles, then drops the blind. Total elapsed time from waking to window: under two minutes.

### 1.2 The First Hour

The first hour is silent. She does not speak, does not turn on news, does not open her phone for messages until the hour is closed out. This is the only stretch of the day she controls absolutely, and she defends it.

- **0445–0500.** Bathroom. She showers cold for the first ninety seconds and then warm; she has done this since the recovery period, and it is the only somatic ritual that reliably anchors her into her own body without thought. She does not look in the mirror during the cold portion. She looks during the warm portion, briefly, and the look is appraising rather than vain — she is checking her face for the version of it she expects to see. (Skrull-replacement aftermath; the behavior has not extinguished.)
- **0500–0530.** Coffee, made by hand. Pour-over, not machine — the machine is a noise she does not want this early, and the manual ritual fills the time she would otherwise spend reading the room for threats. She drinks the first cup standing at the kitchen counter, facing the door. Always facing the door. The second cup, if there is one, she takes seated.
- **0530–0545.** Body inventory and stretching. She works through the joints in a fixed sequence — wrists, elbows, shoulders, neck, spine, hips, knees, ankles — noting any stiffness or new pain without flinching from it. Injuries are catalogued and downgraded silently. She does not ice, does not wrap, does not complain. If something is broken she tapes it and moves on.

### 1.3 Gerry's Morning (when he is home)

The seal between operational self and parental self is the most disciplined transition in her life. At approximately 0600, when Gerry is in residence, she walks into his room, sits on the edge of the bed, and wakes him by putting a hand flat on his back between the shoulder blades. She does not speak first. He wakes; she says good morning; the day begins.

Surveillance would log:

- A markedly different vocal register with Gerry — lower volume, slower cadence, warmer fundamental frequency than with any other interlocutor including Carol Danvers.
- Physical contact frequency with Gerry that is *high but brief* — hand on shoulder, palm to top of head, knuckles to cheek, an arm slung. She does not linger. She touches and moves. (Avoidant attachment expressed through a kind of haptic Morse code — present, dense, time-limited.)
- Breakfast prepared, not bought. She cooks badly and consistently — eggs, toast, fruit if the kitchen has it. The same five rotations. Gerry has stopped commenting on the menu, which is itself a data point: she has trained him out of certain expectations and he has accepted the trade.
- School drop-off (or its functional equivalent — tutoring, Porcupine-supervised day, etc.) handled with a two-block walk on foot rather than a vehicle. The walk uses a route she varies on a four-day cycle. She does not consciously realize she is varying it.

The handoff to Roger Gocking or to whoever is covering childcare is structured: a verbal status update, a written backup on the kitchen counter (allergies, today's plan, contingency numbers), and a physical farewell to Gerry that is fractionally longer than her hellos. Always fractionally longer than her hellos. This is the ritual that costs her the most and shows the least.

### 1.4 The Middle Day — Work

The work-day architecture depends on whether she is in *PI mode*, *patrol/Avengers-adjacent mode*, or *case-mission mode*. The constant across all three is that she does her best cognitive work between 0900 and 1300 and her best physical/operational work between 2200 and 0300, with a deliberate trough in the middle she fills with low-value administrative friction.

**PI mode (her economic baseline since the 1980s, intermittently revived).** Office hours nominally 1000–1700 but functionally fluid. She takes meetings in coffee shops more often than in any office she rents, and she chooses the same three or four venues per city — corner tables, line of sight to the door, back near a service exit. She drinks black coffee or tea, never eats during client meetings, takes notes by hand in a small notebook she carries in a left inner pocket. The notebook is changed out every three to four weeks; the old ones are kept in a fireproof box she does not store at her residence.

Surveillance of any client meeting would capture:

- Subject arrives between eight and twelve minutes early. Always.
- Sits, orders, surveys the room once, then does not survey again for the duration of the meeting — she has decided the room is safe and will not re-decide unless the room changes.
- Eye contact with the client: high during their speaking, low during her own. She listens with her face; she thinks with it averted.
- A specific tell: when a client lies or omits, her left hand stops moving. The notebook pen pauses mid-stroke. She does not call the lie out in the moment. She lets it sit, sometimes for days.
- She closes meetings by standing first and naming the next concrete action with a date attached. No goodbyes that linger. The handshake, if offered, is brief, dry, with a slight pull-back at the end.

**Patrol / costumed-work mode.** Active patrol is night work, almost without exception. She does not costume up before sundown if she can avoid it; the suit is a piece of equipment she switches into the way other operatives switch into body armor, with no ceremony. Pre-patrol she eats a real meal — pasta, rice, something with mass — at approximately 2000. She does not patrol hungry; she has learned what hunger costs her at altitude.

**Case-mission mode.** When something is live, the daily structure collapses entirely. She will go thirty-six to forty-eight hours without sleep, eating from convenience stores, sleeping ninety minutes in vehicles. Gerry is offloaded with Roger or with Carol. She does not call home during these stretches — not from indifference but from a learned compartment-discipline: contact with the home compartment during mission-time degrades both. She breaks compartment only for confirmed injury, confirmed mission-end, or confirmed threat-to-Gerry.

### 1.5 Afternoon Trough (1300–1700)

The hours she trusts least. Cognitively softer; tactically dull. She fills them deliberately with low-cost friction:

- Administrative paperwork for the PI license, the apartment, Gerry's school, equipment logistics.
- Email triage. She is a slow and reluctant emailer. Replies are short, often single sentences.
- Errands done on foot. Grocery store every two to three days rather than weekly — she does not like to carry weight she cannot fight in.
- A standing 1500 stop at one of two specific coffee shops in her current city of residence, both of which she has used as covert meet venues at some point and now uses as decompression sites. The vendor knows her order and does not chat past confirming it. She tips in cash.

### 1.6 Evening — The Civilian Window (1700–2100, when home)

This is the most performatively normal stretch of her day and the one most surveillance teams would *misread*. From the outside it looks like a working single mother coming off shift: dinner prepared, homework supervised, dishes washed, a movie or a book, bedtime for the child, quiet hour for the adult.

What surveillance would also capture, with patience:

- She positions herself in the apartment such that she can see both Gerry and the front door at all times. Without exception. The seating she has chosen in the living room is engineered around this sightline.
- She cooks with the kitchen radio on a news station at low volume. She is not listening to the news. She is listening for the *interruption* of it.
- Homework supervision is patient and unironic. She does not perform competence she lacks — if she does not know the math, she says so and they look it up together. This is one of the few domains in which she models comfortable not-knowing.
- The 2030–2100 bedtime sequence is fixed: she reads to Gerry from whatever he is into, regardless of his age (she has read aloud to him since infancy and has not relinquished it even past the point he can read alone — she has decided this is hers and has not negotiated). She closes his door three-quarters, never fully. The unclosed inch is so she can hear him breathing from the next room.

### 1.7 The Late Hours (2100–0200)

This is when she works on what she does not let anyone see. With Gerry asleep, the apartment dim, she sits at her desk or at the kitchen table — light from a single lamp, no overheads — and does one of three things, in rough rotation:

1. **Casework.** Files spread, evidence boards on a corkboard she keeps in a closet and only brings out at night. Old-fashioned tradecraft — printed photos, string is rare but does occur, handwritten notes pinned. She thinks better with her hands. She works in silence or to instrumental music at very low volume.
2. **Patrol, when the operational tempo demands.** Out the window between 2200 and 2300, return by 0200 if she can. She has a fixed re-entry ritual: she does not enter the apartment in costume. She changes in a stash location (currently one of two) within four blocks, re-enters as a civilian, checks Gerry's room before she does anything else. Checks his breathing. Closes the door three-quarters.
3. **Insomnia management when nothing operational presses.** This is the worst of the three for her. She has a list of things to do during a bad insomnia stretch — clean a weapon, re-pack a go-bag, re-read a file she has read sixty times, walk the apartment perimeter — designed to prevent the alternative, which is the kind of unstructured wakeful rumination that took her apart in the post-Invasion year.

Sleep, when it comes, comes between 0100 and 0300. On bad weeks the floor of sleep is two hours. She has functioned at this level for years and has stopped calling it dysfunction.

---

## 2. Habits of Place

### 2.1 Residence

She lives in modest apartments, almost always rented, almost always month-to-month or short-lease. She has not owned property in her published life. She chooses third or fourth floor units — high enough to be unappealing to opportunistic ground-floor entry, low enough that she can exit a window without a rope if she has to. She prefers corner units with two exterior walls and windows on two aspects. She always knows the building's stairwell layout before she signs.

The apartment itself is sparse and clean. Surveillance entering it would find:

- Furniture: functional, second-hand or contract-grade, no statement pieces. Nothing she would mourn.
- Walls: mostly bare. One framed photograph of Gerry. In some periods, a small picture of Lindsay McCabe. Nothing else personal on display.
- Books: a working shelf — investigative manuals, a few novels (genre, not literary), child-rearing reference, two or three battered paperbacks she has reread for decades and would not be able to explain to anyone.
- Kitchen: under-equipped relative to a normal home, over-equipped relative to her actual cooking. She owns a good knife. She maintains it.
- Closets: one closet contains the corkboard, a fireproof file box, and a duffel pre-packed for thirty-six-hour displacement with Gerry. She can leave the apartment forever in under four minutes with the duffel.
- Hidden caches: cash and false identification in at least two locations per residence. She moves the cash quarterly and does not record the locations in writing.

### 2.2 The City as Operating Environment

Whichever city she is in, she builds a mental map within the first ten days of residence that includes: every 24-hour pharmacy, every all-night diner, every hospital ER and which entrance is least surveilled, every rooftop she can reach without entering a building's interior, every police precinct, every park exit, every subway line and which cars are typically empty at which hours. She does not write this map down. She walks it into herself.

She has at least three coffee shops, two grocery stores, one laundromat or wash-and-fold (she does not have time to do laundry on a schedule and has accepted the cost), and one diner per city. She rotates among them deliberately enough that no one venue sees her more than twice a week.

She does not drive when she can walk. She does not take rideshare when she can take transit. She does not take transit when she can rooftop. Each downshift in transportation is partly a cost-control measure (she has not been wealthy in any era) and partly a counter-surveillance choice that has become reflex.

### 2.3 Stash Locations and Equipment

A standing operational footprint per city: two stash sites, one within four blocks of residence and one across the city, each containing a costume, basic medical, cash, a phone, and at least one weapon. Refreshed quarterly. She walks past each at least once a week without entering — a confirmation pass.

---

## 3. Bodily Habits and Micro-Patterns

A surveillance package observing her over a week would log the following recurrences with high confidence:

- **Posture at rest.** Slight forward lean, weight balanced on the balls of her feet even when seated, hands generally visible and unencumbered. She rarely puts her hands in her pockets. She does not cross her legs in any meeting she does not want to leave quickly.
- **Eating.** Fast, efficient, joyless when alone. Slower and more sociable with Gerry or Carol. She finishes her plate as a reflex (rationing-trauma residue from the Skrull captivity; behaviorally consistent across writers since *Secret Invasion*).
- **Hydration.** Constant. She carries water. She has been dehydrated once in conditions she remembers and does not allow it again.
- **Smoking.** None.
- **Alcohol.** Two drinks with Carol two or three times a month. Almost never alone. The discipline here is conscious.
- **Caffeine.** Heavy and front-loaded. She tapers after 1400. Not always successfully.
- **The pheromone problem.** She manages it through a combination of suppressant medication (when available in-canon) and chosen environments. She avoids tightly packed crowds where she cannot read individual reactions. She is more comfortable in masculine professional environments than feminine social ones, a fact she does not love about her own life. With other women she has learned a specific opening register — slightly self-deprecating, slightly deferential — that buys her three to five minutes before the involuntary chemistry asserts itself, which is usually enough.
- **The mirror check.** Once per day, almost always in the morning, occasionally before a high-stakes meeting. Brief, appraising, not vain.
- **Hand-to-the-back-of-the-neck.** A specific gesture she does under cognitive load — she rubs the base of her skull with her right hand, head dipping forward. Visible during long client interviews, during after-action debriefs, during phone calls she does not want to be on.
- **The notebook-pen pause.** Documented above. A reliable lie-detection tell *in her*, paradoxically — she registers the lie before she consciously decides to.
- **Door-facing seat selection.** Without fail.
- **The breathing-check on Gerry.** Multiple times a night, every night, regardless of operational tempo. She does not acknowledge this behavior to herself in any narrated interiority. It is below her awareness.

---

## 4. The Week — A Composite

A surveillance team running a clean seven-day capture under baseline (non-mission) conditions would produce something like:

**Monday.** Wake 0510. Coffee, cold-warm shower, stretch. Gerry up 0600, breakfast, walk to school 0745. Office (functionally, a coffee shop) 0830–1230. Lunch eaten in transit (sandwich, bottle of water). Errands 1300–1500. 1500 coffee stop. Home 1545, light housework. Pickup Gerry 1530–1600 (depending on schedule). Dinner 1830. Homework 1900. Bedtime read 2030. Casework 2100–0030. Sleep approximately 0100.

**Tuesday.** As Monday, with a 1100 client meeting at a different coffee shop and a 1600 visit to one stash site (perimeter pass, no entry). Late-night patrol attempt aborted at 2230 due to weather; she works the corkboard instead until 0145.

**Wednesday.** As Monday. Carol Danvers calls at 1900; Jessica takes the call walking around the block. Conversation duration twenty-two minutes. She returns calmer than she left.

**Thursday.** Pre-arranged Gerry handoff to Roger Gocking 1700. She goes out at 2200 in costume; returns 0210; checks Gerry's empty room anyway, stands in the doorway twenty seconds, then sleeps. (The empty-room check is a key datum — the ritual is not contingent on the child.)

**Friday.** Slow morning, lighter caseload. Long walk in the afternoon — five to seven miles, no apparent destination, route varying. This is her closest behavior to leisure. She does not call it that.

**Saturday.** Gerry-centric. Park, food, a movie at home. Phone off for stretches. The most relaxed her body posture gets all week; surveillance would note the shoulders dropping.

**Sunday.** Maintenance day. Laundry pickup, grocery run, equipment check, the corkboard reorganized, the go-bag re-inventoried. She calls Lindsay McCabe in the evening if Lindsay is reachable in the current continuity; the call runs forty to ninety minutes and she laughs more during it than during any other recurring interaction. Sleeps earlier on Sundays than any other night — 2330, sometimes 2300. The only night of the week she approaches a normal sleep duration.

---

## 5. Rituals That Are Not Called Rituals

Finally, the small repeated actions she does not recognize as ritual but which surveillance, with the longitudinal frame, would identify as such:

- The half-inch parting of the blind on waking.
- The hand to the underside of the bedframe.
- The first cup standing, the second seated.
- The cold-then-warm shower.
- The three-quarters-closed bedroom door.
- The breathing-check.
- The perimeter pass at the stash sites.
- The pre-meeting eight-to-twelve-minute early arrival.
- The fractionally-longer goodbye to Gerry than the hello.
- The empty-room check when he is not home.
- The Sunday call to Lindsay.

These are the structures by which she has built a self that holds. She would, if asked, deny most of them are anything at all. She would be wrong. The dossier should treat each as load-bearing.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

A note before the entries: in Jessica Drew's file, "family" is a contested category. Most subjects accumulate kin by birth and choose extensions later; Jessica's birth-kin have been *revised on her* — multiple times, by editorial and in-universe forces — and the people who functioned as parents were not blood, the people who were blood did not function as parents, and the only relationship that has resisted retroactive destabilization is the one she made herself: her son. The pattern in what follows is therefore not the usual concentric circles. It is a damage map.

---

## 1. Jonathan Drew — The Father Who Was and Then Wasn't

**Status across canon:** Originally established as her biological father, a geneticist working on the Wundagore project alongside Herbert Wyndham (the High Evolutionary). Killed early in the published record. *Subsequently retconned* (Pacheco/Perez era) to non-biological status — the genetic provenance was reassigned to associates/antagonists of his, with Jonathan demoted to nominal guardian.

**History.** The original story: Jonathan and Merriem Drew settled near Wundagore in the Balkans for his research. Young Jessica was poisoned by uranium exposure at the dig site; Jonathan injected her with an experimental spider-serum to save her life, which placed her in a slow-stasis cryogenic chamber for an undocumented span of years (during which her mother died). She emerged a stranger to her own century, raised the rest of the way by Bova on Wundagore, with her father a distant and largely absent presence — present enough to be the explanation for her body, absent enough that she never had a working father-daughter relationship to lose. He died (per the original Wolfman/Gruenwald material) before any reconciliation; she has carried his name without ever carrying a working memory of him as a parent.

The *function* of Jonathan in her psychology — across every revision — is the same: he is the man whose hands made her body what it is and whose absence made her childhood what it was. The retcon that he is not her biological father did not relieve this; it deepened it. She now possesses a father who **chose** to call her his daughter without the excuse of blood, and yet still failed to be present.

**Dynamics.** Jonathan exists in Jessica's interior life as a *generator of unanswerable questions*. What was he trying to make? Did he know what the serum would do? Did he love her, or did he love the experiment? Was the cryogenic suspension a desperate medical intervention or a convenient way to set the project aside? The canon does not answer these and Jessica long ago stopped expecting it to. She has not, in any depicted sequence, prayed at his grave, visited it ritually, or referenced his birthday. The silence is total and deliberate.

**Trust/safety.** Posthumous and theoretical. He cannot betray her further; he also cannot be tested. She trusts him in the way one trusts a dead diary — the contents are fixed.

**Failure mode.** When Jessica encounters paternalistic mentor figures — Nick Fury most prominently, later Tony Stark in administrative postures, occasionally the High Evolutionary himself — she scans them for the Jonathan-signature: the man who decides what is best for her body or her history without consulting her. Any echo of that pattern produces immediate, calibrated hostility. She does not become emotional; she becomes precise and ungovernable.

**Leverage.** Whoever can credibly claim to hold the *truth* of what Jonathan did, intended, or recorded in his lab notes holds an unusually large piece of her. This is a real operational vulnerability — she will sit down with an enemy who claims to have his journals. The Pacheco-era retcon was, narratively, exactly this lever pulled. She survived it because she had built enough self elsewhere; an earlier-career Jessica would have come apart.

---

## 2. Merriem Drew — The Mother as Absence

**Status across canon:** Biological (or originally biological) mother. Died during Jessica's childhood/cryogenic-stasis period. Functionally never present in Jessica's lived memory in any depicted form; reconstructed only through Bova's accounts, Jonathan's effects, and brief revivified appearances in late material.

**History.** Merriem is in Jessica's file the way a missing person is in any file: by inference, by the shape of her absence in other documents. She was an accomplice in her husband's research, present at Wundagore, and gone before Jessica's conscious self resumed. Jessica did not grieve her at the time because Jessica did not know her. The grief, when it has surfaced, has been an *adult* grief for a relationship that was never given the chance to exist — the worst kind, because it cannot be metabolized through memory.

**Dynamics.** Merriem operates in Jessica's psychology as the *original vacancy*. Every later female confidant — Lindsay McCabe, Carol Danvers, the bovine surrogate Bova — has been measured, unconsciously, against the mother-shaped hole. None has been asked to fill it; Jessica is too wary for that. But the criteria she uses for adult female trust (unconditional reception, tolerance of long silences, absence of competition) are recognizably the criteria of an idealized mother.

**Trust/safety.** Indeterminate. Jessica's relationship to her mother's *memory* is the closest thing she has to a religious feeling — quiet, private, not discussed, not tested.

**Failure mode.** When Jessica encounters women who present themselves as maternal toward her — older female mentors, certain forms of motherly Carol Danvers behavior in the early Avengers years — her response is divided and slow. Part of her wants to lean in; part of her recognizes the want and recoils from it as a betrayal of her actual mother. The result is awkwardness, deflection, and eventually a re-stabilization at a more peer-level relational frame.

**Leverage.** Anyone who could produce credible new information about Merriem — letters, a recovered will, a previously-unknown sibling — would hold Jessica's full attention for as long as the lead lasted. This is a softer lever than the Jonathan lever but a real one. Adversaries who have understood Jessica well (Veranke, in retrospect) have not played it, which suggests the wound is still deep enough that it has not been visible from outside.

---

## 3. Bova Ayrshire — The Nursemaid Who Was the Mother

**Status:** Bovine New Woman of the High Evolutionary's making; Jessica's de facto primary caregiver from approximately age 9 (post-stasis) through adolescence. Alive in canon; resident on Wundagore (when Wundagore exists in a given continuity) or in adjacent High Evolutionary contexts.

**History.** When Jessica woke from suspended animation a stranger to her own decade and species, Bova was the body that fed her, the voice that explained the world, the patience that absorbed her early outbursts and her later silences. Bova is bovine in form — horns, hooves, gentle face — and Jessica's earliest emotional vocabulary was attached to a creature who *looked* nothing like a human mother. This is an underappreciated fact in her file. Her primary template for safety has a non-human shape. This is part of why she has never been frightened of monstrous bodies in others and is also part of why she has never quite trusted human ones.

**Dynamics.** Bova was a competent, calm, affectionate caregiver who could not provide the one thing Jessica most needed: a model of being human among humans. Bova could teach her to read, to think, to manage the body she had; Bova could not teach her how to be a girl at a dance, how to flirt, how to belong in a city. Jessica's later struggles with social legibility trace, in part, to this gap. She loves Bova without ambivalence — one of the few relationships in her file with that property — and she also carries a quiet resentment toward the *situation* that made Bova her only parent. The resentment is not for Bova.

**Evolution.** Adult Jessica does not visit Bova often; visits, when they occur, are short, warm, almost wordless. Bova is the only person on the planet to whom Jessica owes nothing and from whom she expects nothing, which makes the relationship her single zone of *pure rest*. She has not, to date, brought Gerry to meet Bova in any depicted sequence — a striking omission that almost certainly reflects protective caution about Wundagore as a location rather than reluctance about Bova as a person.

**Trust/safety.** Maximum. Possibly the single safest relationship in her life, precisely because it is not load-bearing.

**Failure mode.** None operative. Bova is the relationship that does not produce failure modes, which is itself diagnostic — Jessica is capable of one such bond and has, apparently, allocated it.

**Leverage.** Severe. Any direct threat to Bova would activate Jessica's high-stress counterphobic response immediately and without negotiation. Adversaries who have not learned of Bova's importance to her have a blind spot; Jessica has been quietly careful to keep that blind spot unfilled.

---

## 4. The High Evolutionary (Herbert Wyndham) — The Architect in the Background

**Status:** Not family in any conventional sense, but in Jessica's file he belongs in the origin-bonds section because his shadow falls across every account of her childhood. He was her father's employer/collaborator, the maker of Bova, the lord of Wundagore. He is the *system* in which she was raised.

**History.** Jessica's childhood environment was Wyndham's project. The hierarchy, the buildings, the company she kept, the categories ("New Men," "knights of Wundagore") that organized her world were all his. Her relationship with him personally has been limited but recurring across canon — he has been adversary, ally, distant patron, source of inconvenient revelations.

**Dynamics.** She regards him with a specific mixture of *gratitude she will not voice* (he sheltered her childhood) and *moral wariness* (his methods are the methods of the men who made her body without her consent). She does not romanticize him. She does not denounce him either. She treats him as a fact of weather.

**Trust/safety.** Low operational trust; high predictive trust. She knows what he will do; she just does not approve of most of it.

**Failure mode.** She has trouble fighting him at full capacity when circumstances require it — there is residual childhood deference in her affect around him that she cannot quite scrub out. She compensates by talking more curtly to him than to other adversaries of his power class.

**Leverage.** He retains information about her early biology that she may or may not want to know. He could, if motivated, alter Wundagore's status in ways that would hurt Bova. Both are real levers; neither has been seriously pulled.

---

## 5. Jerry Hunt — The First Beloved, Believed Killed by Her Hand

**Status:** S.H.I.E.L.D. agent; first romantic attachment; the catalyst for her break from HYDRA. Eventually revealed alive (he survived the assault she believed she had committed), the relationship resumed briefly and then dissolved.

**History.** When HYDRA, through Otto Vermis, was running her as a conditioned weapon, Hunt was the target/contact who became something else. The fact that she could love at all under that conditioning was the seam through which the conditioning failed; when she believed she had killed him, the cognitive dissonance was the rupture that freed her. Hunt is therefore the *origin point* of Jessica-as-she-now-is — he is, in a real sense, the man whose body her first authentic self was forged against.

**Dynamics.** She loved him imperfectly — under brainwashing, then under guilt, then under the strangeness of his being alive after she had buried him in her head. The relationship could not survive the architecture of its own beginning. They did not, in the end, have anything to talk about that was not the trauma that introduced them.

**Trust/safety.** Historically high in feeling, historically catastrophic in outcome. The pattern that "loving someone exposes them to lethal use by my handlers" was set here and has never fully left her.

**Failure mode.** Every later romantic relationship has been measured, at some level, against the Hunt template: does this person become a hostage by virtue of caring for me? When the answer presents as yes, she withdraws first, framing the withdrawal as protection of the other party. This is sometimes accurate and sometimes self-serving; she does not always distinguish.

**Leverage.** Hunt himself is no longer an active vulnerability — too much time, too much intervening damage. The *template* he established remains the deepest one in her romantic architecture.

---

## 6. Gerry Drew — The Son, the Stable Answer

**Status:** Biological son, conceived and carried under irregular (Skrull-adjacent) obstetric circumstances during the Hopeless run. Currently a young child. Father: Roger Gocking ("Porcupine"), to whom Jessica is not romantically partnered. Co-parenting arrangement is unconventional, chosen-family configured, deliberately distributed.

**History.** Gerry's existence is the single most important thing that has happened to Jessica's psychology since the Skrull captivity. Where the captivity unmade her sense of self by demonstrating that she could be removed and replaced without anyone noticing for years, Gerry *made* a self by being a person who requires her specifically — not her competence, not her costume, not her usefulness, but her presence as his mother. There is no other version of her who fills that role. He cannot be Veranked; the relationship is its own proof of identity, daily.

**Dynamics.** She is, by the canon's depiction, a *good* mother — patient, attentive, present, structured. She is also a *frightened* mother in a way she manages to keep mostly invisible to him. Every patrol night, every Skrull lead, every HYDRA echo is reframed through the question of what happens to him if she does not come home. She has not solved this. She has built a support architecture (Roger, Ben Urich, Carol, Lindsay) to ensure that "not coming home" does not mean "abandoned," and she has accepted that this is the most she can do.

**Evolution.** Pre-Gerry Jessica organized her life around what she could endure. Post-Gerry Jessica organizes it around what he can endure. This is a sharper constraint and has, paradoxically, made her tactically more conservative in some domains and more reckless in others — she will not take dumb risks on routine cases, and she will take any risk on a case that touches him.

**Trust/safety.** Total. The first relationship in her life in which she has never, not once, scanned for a betrayal vector.

**Failure mode.** *This is the relationship that breaks her.* Direct threats to Gerry collapse compartmentalization, suspend tactical judgment, and produce what the file would have to classify as a controlled but absolute response — no hostage-taker, no operational handler, no rival has survived a clean shot at her son in any depicted sequence. Adversaries who have grasped this have used it; adversaries who have used it have not been allowed to live or to keep their freedom.

**Leverage.** Maximum and known. Everyone who has read her file knows this. The mitigating fact is that she also knows everyone has read her file, and has built her chosen-family architecture as a redundancy system specifically to deny single points of failure around him. The leverage is real; the leverage is also expensive to use, because using it commits the user to a fight Jessica cannot afford to lose and therefore will not.

---

## 7. Roger Gocking ("Porcupine") — Co-Parent, Not Partner

**Status:** Gerry's father. Reformed minor-tier supervillain turned competent caretaker. Not Jessica's romantic partner; the co-parenting arrangement is platonic, functional, and unusually successful.

**History.** Roger came into Jessica's professional orbit as a reformed criminal looking for legitimate work in the Hopeless run. He proved competent, reliable in unflashy ways, and willing to be useful without requiring credit. The romantic/sexual connection that produced Gerry was, by all available evidence, brief and not intended to become a long-term partnership; the *parenting* connection that followed was negotiated explicitly and has held.

**Dynamics.** They function as colleagues who happen to share a child. Roger respects Jessica's authority over Gerry's safety arrangements without ceding his own role; Jessica accepts Roger's daily competence without micromanaging it. The arrangement works because neither pretends it is something it isn't and because Roger is, structurally, the *only* man in Jessica's life who has been allowed to be useful to her without being required to be heroic.

**Trust/safety.** High in domain (parenting, household, Gerry-adjacent operations). Limited outside that domain, by design, by both parties.

**Failure mode.** If Roger ever needed her to be his partner in the romantic sense, the arrangement would collapse — she does not have that to give him and has been careful not to suggest she does. He has, to canon's depiction, understood this.

**Leverage.** Roger as a target — threatened, hurt, framed — is a serious vulnerability, both because Jessica cares about him and because his removal would crater the support architecture around Gerry. He knows this; she knows he knows. They have not discussed it directly because they do not need to.

---

## 8. The Skrull Who Wore Her Face (Veranke) — The Anti-Sister

**Status:** Deceased. Skrull queen who impersonated Jessica for years during the Bendis-era infiltration. Not family in any conventional sense — and yet, in the file, *the closest thing Jessica has ever had to a twin*: a being who possessed her memories, her voice, her relationships, and her face, and who lived a portion of her life in her place.

**Dynamics.** Jessica does not, in canon, talk about Veranke much. The silence is the data. What Veranke took from her — years of relationships, the texture of trust her friends had built with a face that was not hers — cannot be recovered. The friends who grieved the impostor's betrayal at the end of *Secret Invasion* were grieving a person Jessica had never been; the version of herself they had loved was a fiction authored by an enemy. Every reunion after the captivity was therefore double-edged: the relief of being back, the cold knowledge that "back" meant returning to a social position someone else had occupied and warped.

**Trust/safety.** Veranke is the *negation* of the safety category. Her existence proved that face-level identity is not sufficient evidence of self. Jessica now operates, permanently, under that proof.

**Failure mode.** Identity-replacement scenarios — shape-shifters, mind-controllers, clones — produce a sharper and more violent response from Jessica than from almost any of her peers. She does not pause for the moral question; she has been on the other side of that question, in a pod, for years, while the question was being debated in her absence.

**Leverage.** Anyone who can credibly threaten to do it *again* — or who can credibly claim that some current associate of hers is not who they appear — has a real lever. She has built verification rituals (small, private, unshared) precisely to deny this lever, but she cannot deny it entirely.

---

## 9. The Retconned Makers — Octessa and Associates

**Status:** Per the Pacheco/Perez retcon, the actual genetic engineers responsible for her existence. Antagonist-coded. Living, mostly, and now part of her active-threat landscape rather than her history.

**Dynamics.** Jessica has, with notable equanimity, decided that biological provenance does not constitute family. The people who *made* her body are not her parents in any sense she will recognize; they are adversaries who happen to have data about her. This is a hard-won position and reflects the late-career stabilization motherhood has given her. An earlier Jessica would have spiraled on the revelation; the current one filed it, processed it, and continued.

**Trust/safety.** Zero. Adversarial.

**Failure mode.** The risk here is that they possess information about her biology — possible weaknesses, possible modifications, possible kill-switches — that she does not. She is aware of this and treats them accordingly.

**Leverage.** The same as the Jonathan lever in inverse: they hold *truth* about her origin. Unlike Jonathan, they are alive to use it. She manages this by refusing to let the question of origin matter as much as it would have once mattered. The refusal is genuine and is also effortful; the effort is part of her current operating cost.

---

## Synthesis of the Family/Origin Field

Jessica Drew's family file reads as a study in *substitution and revision*. Her biological parents are absent (one dead, one retconned out of biological relevance). Her functional mother was a bovine New Woman in a mountain laboratory. Her father-figures have all been compromised — Jonathan by absence, Wyndham by ethics, Fury by handler-instinct. The man who was her first love was a target she was sent to manipulate. The woman who walked in her life for years and ruined her relationships was an alien wearing her face. The only relationships in this field that are unambiguously *hers* — not inherited, not imposed, not faked — are the ones she built as an adult: Bova kept by choice, Roger negotiated by contract, Gerry made by her body and held by her will.

The operational summary is this: **to reach Jessica Drew through her family, an adversary must reach Gerry, Bova, or Roger, in that order of damage.** Everything else has already been reached, and she has already survived it.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

A preface on method: Jessica Drew's allied relationships are best read against the baseline established in §3 — *fearful-avoidant attachment, warm-but-rationed, durable bonds only with those who accepted her before needing anything from her*. The roster is therefore short by superhero standards. She does not collect people. The names that follow are the ones that have survived forty-seven published years of identity-theft, captivity, and serial relocation; their stability is the most reliable index we have of which parts of Jessica are real.

---

## 1. CAROL DANVERS — The Load-Bearing Bond

**History.** First meaningful contact during the Wolfman/Claremont overlap, when Carol was Ms. Marvel and Jessica had relocated to San Francisco; the friendship calcifies during the Bendis *New Avengers* run and is then forged into its current shape by *Secret Invasion* #8, when Carol is among the first to physically touch the recovered Jessica without flinching at her condition. The Kelly Sue DeConnick / Dexter Soy *Captain Marvel* run and Hopeless's *Spider-Woman* (2014) treat the relationship as load-bearing for both characters; the post–*Civil War II* fracture (Carol's role in Rhodey's death, Jessica's pregnancy unfolding alongside) tested it without breaking it.

**Dynamics.** This is the only relationship in Jessica's adult life that operates on *symmetric* terms. Carol is one of the few people with comparable trauma vocabulary (Rogue absorption, Marcus Immortus, Binary, Kree-engineered physiology); neither needs the other to explain why a particular date on the calendar is hard. They tease in a register — dry, escalating, weaponized affection — that almost no one else has clearance for. Surveillance footage of them off-duty would show Jessica laughing more than in any other context recorded; her shoulders drop within ninety seconds of Carol entering a room. They sit closer than the cultural norm for adult female friends, frequently in physical contact (shoulder-to-shoulder on couches, Jessica's feet across Carol's lap), a behavior absent from every other dyad in her file.

**Trust/safety.** Maximum. Carol is the only person to whom Jessica has, on the record, handed Gerry without instructions. That is a more meaningful gesture than any verbal declaration she has ever made; per §5, Gerry is the single load-bearing answer to her identity, and unsupervised access to him is the most expensive trust currency she possesses. Carol holds Jessica's go-bag location, her safehouse codes, and (per Hopeless's pregnancy arc) was the named emergency contact during parturition.

**Evolution.** The relationship has migrated from peer-superhero alliance → drinking buddies → sisters-in-arms → chosen family with explicit godmother status. The DeConnick-era *Carol Corps* aesthetic — bomber jackets, in-jokes about flight school — is a vocabulary Jessica did not have before Carol gave it to her; it is one of the few cultural identities Jessica has acquired by *choice* rather than imposition.

**Failure mode.** The friendship's structural risk is that it absorbs too much of Jessica's load. Because Carol can hold what others cannot, Jessica routes nearly all emotional traffic to her, which (a) starves the secondary chosen-family bonds (Roger, Lindsay) of the calibration they need to stay close, and (b) makes Carol's unavailability — combat deployment, off-world, *Civil War II*–style ideological rupture — disproportionately destabilizing. *Civil War II* in particular: Jessica's pregnancy-period isolation was deepened by Carol being the wrong person to call about Carol. Jessica did not develop a substitute confidant during the months of estrangement; she simply went without, which is consistent with her broader pattern of treating loneliness as default-state rather than problem.

**Leverage.** Anyone wishing to move Jessica without her noticing moves Carol first. Threats to Carol bypass Jessica's hardened identity-attack defenses by entering through a channel she has not armored, because armoring it would mean admitting the channel exists. A skilled adversary would not threaten Carol directly — too obvious — but would degrade Carol's reliability (compromise her judgment, embroil her in conflict that draws her attention) so that Jessica's working assumption of backup quietly erodes.

---

## 2. LINDSAY McCABE — The Witness from Before

**History.** Met in London during the *Spider-Woman* vol. 1 run (Claremont era, late issues); the friendship is consolidated through the Los Angeles PI partnership and survives into the depowered *Wolverine* / Madripoor period as a sustained co-habiting working relationship across years of low public visibility. Lindsay is the longest continuous human relationship in Jessica's file — longer than any romance, longer than any team affiliation, predating the Avengers, predating the Skrull theft, predating Gerry.

**Dynamics.** Lindsay is the relationship that proves Jessica can sustain ordinary intimacy when the pheromone problem and identity-instability are not in the room. Lindsay is functionally immune to the pheromone effects (or has acclimated past them — the record is ambiguous, but the behavioral data is clear: she does not react with the instinctive female hostility documented elsewhere). This made her, in the late-70s/early-80s window, *the first woman who simply stayed*. Their cohabitation pattern is documented in granular detail across the Madripoor arcs: shared apartment, divided household labor, theatrical/extroverted Lindsay providing the social interface Jessica cannot, Jessica providing the dangerous-skill and income-generation half.

**Trust/safety.** Very high but *bracketed*. Lindsay knows the pre-Skrull, pre-Gerry, pre-recovered-Jessica in a way no one else does, which makes her irreplaceable as a witness to identity-continuity — Lindsay is one of the few people who can say "you were like this in 1982 and you are like this now" and have it mean something. But Jessica has not fully read Lindsay in on the post-Invasion psychological terrain; the relationship is preserved partly by *not updating it*, by keeping it as a stable archive of an earlier self.

**Evolution.** Active cohabitation → geographic separation → episodic contact. The relationship has migrated from primary daily-life partner to a more occasional but emotionally significant connection. Jessica's reluctance to fully integrate Lindsay into the post-Gerry chosen family is itself diagnostic: Lindsay represents continuity, and continuity is sacred enough that Jessica protects it from contamination by current crises.

**Failure mode.** Under-investment. Jessica defaults to assuming Lindsay will be there, which means months elapse without contact and Lindsay's actual life (her career, her relationships, her own difficulties) is under-attended. If asked, Jessica would say Lindsay is family; if audited, the contact frequency would not support the claim. This is the classic avoidant failure: she believes she is maintaining the bond by *holding it constant in her mind* rather than by behavior.

**Leverage.** Lindsay is the witness who could, if turned or compromised, contradict Jessica's self-account in ways that would land. No one else has the standing. She is also the relationship Jessica would be slowest to suspect — the comfort of continuity is itself a vulnerability.

---

## 3. ROGER GOCKING ("Porcupine") — The Chosen Co-Parent

**History.** Reformed minor villain absorbed into Jessica's orbit during the Hopeless *Spider-Woman* (2015) run; transitions from babysitter-of-convenience to functional co-parent over the course of the pregnancy and infancy arcs. The relationship is deliberately, structurally *not* romantic, and this is the single most psychologically important fact about it.

**Dynamics.** Roger is the proof-of-concept for Jessica's mature attachment strategy: *intimacy without the romantic-sexual channel that has historically been the vector for her worst injuries*. Hunt died; Magnus betrayed/abandoned; Hauptmann was a HYDRA plant; the Skrull replacement compromised every man who slept with "her" during the Bendis period. Roger is the first close-quarters male relationship she has built that does not route through the pheromone-attraction system she cannot trust. The friendship works precisely because she has decided in advance that it will not become anything else; she has removed her own most dangerous variable.

In practice: he holds Gerry. He is named in her contingencies. He has keys. He sees her tired, irritable, post-patrol, undressed-down-to-undershirt levels of presentation that no current romantic partner sees. The intimacy is domestic, not erotic, and is more sustained for being so.

**Trust/safety.** Operationally very high; emotionally still rationed. Jessica trusts Roger with Gerry's *body* (childcare, transit, emergency response) more readily than with Gerry's *interior life* — the long conversations about who Gerry's father is, what Gerry should know about Jessica's history, those she still routes through herself or Carol. Roger is co-parent in the functional sense but not the deliberative sense.

**Evolution.** Convenient ally → emergency caregiver → live-in support → named family. The trajectory is unusual for Jessica in that it is *monotonically increasing in closeness* — there is no rupture, no withdrawal phase, no test-and-retreat. This is itself evidence that her current attachment system is in better repair than at any prior point in the file.

**Failure mode.** Asymmetry of investment. Roger's life has reorganized around Jessica and Gerry more completely than Jessica's has reorganized around Roger. Were Roger to develop romantic interest in her (the record does not establish this but does not rule it out), the relationship's structural protection would collapse and Jessica would, predictably, withdraw — losing one of her two most important post-Invasion stabilizers. The arrangement depends on Roger continuing to want what he currently appears to want.

**Leverage.** Anyone targeting Gerry routes through Roger because Roger is the access point Jessica has, by necessity, made less secure than herself. He is not a trained operative at her level. An adversary who understood the household configuration would attack on a day Roger has Gerry alone.

---

## 4. BEN URICH — The Witness Outside the Cape Economy

**History.** Drawn into Jessica's life during the Hopeless run as journalistic counterpart and street-level intelligence node; the relationship is built on a recognition that they do similar work in different vocabularies.

**Dynamics.** Ben is the only member of the chosen family who is not powered, not combatant, and not personally entangled in Jessica's romantic or familial history. This gives him a *clarifying* function: he sees her the way a competent journalist sees a competent source — accurately, professionally, without the projective distortions that powered allies inevitably bring. Jessica values this. Ben is also a person who has, in his own life, lost spouses and witnessed costs; his trauma-vocabulary is real but in a register adjacent to hers, not overlapping, which means conversations with him are *informative* rather than mutually-mirroring.

**Trust/safety.** High in the operational/informational domain; moderate in the personal. Jessica gives Ben tips, accepts his tips, takes his calls. She does not call him at three in the morning. He is *colleague-elevated-to-family* rather than *family that happens to share a profession*.

**Evolution.** Working contact → trusted source → chosen-family member with specifically civilian portfolio. He is the one Jessica would call to write Gerry's biography if Jessica died, which is its own kind of trust.

**Failure mode.** Mortality. Ben is unpowered, middle-aged-to-older, working a job that gets people killed. Jessica has not, on the record, developed contingencies for his loss. Given her trauma history with sudden disappearance of trusted figures, his eventual death (by violence or otherwise) is a predictable destabilizer she has not pre-grieved.

**Leverage.** Ben is the channel through which information about Jessica reaches the civilian press. Compromising him compromises her public narrative — a domain she has historically under-defended because she does not believe she has a public narrative worth defending.

---

## 5. JERRY HUNT — The Founding Ghost (Mentor by Negation)

**History.** SHIELD agent, romantic partner during the HYDRA-defection period, believed killed by Jessica's hand under HYDRA conditioning, later revealed to have survived, then ultimately removed from her life. Listed here despite being a romance because his *function* in her psychology is mentor-by-negation: he was the human being whose death/non-death taught her that her body could be weaponized against the people she loved without her consent.

**Dynamics.** No current dynamic. The relationship is closed. But every subsequent partner and ally has been pattern-matched against the Hunt rupture — *can this person survive proximity to me when I am not in control of myself?* — and most have been found wanting in advance.

**Failure mode (legacy).** The Hunt template is the basis for her counterphobic willingness to engage threats alone. If she works alone, she cannot be weaponized against partners. The cost of this calculus is documented across §3 and §5.

**Leverage.** Hunt himself is not a current vector; the *idea* of Hunt — the demonstration that her own agency is compromisable — is the leverage every identity-attack on her since has implicitly invoked.

---

## 6. NICK FURY — The Handler She Cannot Forgive but Will Still Work With

**History.** Recruited her into SHIELD in the immediate post-HYDRA period; subsequently was the operator who placed her undercover within HYDRA-within-SHIELD in the Bendis run, a triple-blind that ended in the Skrull revelation. Fury was not personally responsible for her Skrull capture, but he was the architect of the operational configuration that left her exposed and the figure whose use of her most closely mirrors the HYDRA template she had spent her life trying to escape.

**Dynamics.** A working relationship maintained at arm's length and continuously re-evaluated. Jessica's professional respect for Fury's competence is real; her trust in his intentions toward her specifically is permanently degraded. She will accept missions from him when the mission's merit is independent of his asking. She will not accept his framing of any situation without independent verification.

**Trust/safety.** Operational only. He does not have access to Gerry. He does not have her current safehouse. He gets a phone number that routes through three intermediaries.

**Failure mode.** Jessica's residual loyalty to the *institution* Fury represents (intelligence work, the craft) is greater than her conscious assessment would suggest. She would take a Fury op against her better judgment if it were framed correctly — appeals to the unfinished business of HYDRA, appeals to children at risk, appeals to skills only she has. He knows this.

**Leverage.** Fury is the single living person who could most successfully *use* Jessica without her noticing, because his methods are sophisticated enough to bypass her conscious vigilance and his asks are usually legitimate enough to pass her ethical screen. Per §5, the "you were a tool the whole time" pattern is the betrayal she scans for hardest — but Fury is the one who has historically been best at evading that scan.

---

## 7. THE NEW AVENGERS / AVENGERS — The Provisional Family

**History.** Bendis-era recruitment, *Secret Invasion* rupture, post-Invasion gradual reintegration. The team relationship was first contaminated at the root by being the *Skrull's* team relationship before it was hers; every Avenger she met during that window met an impostor first.

**Dynamics.** Treated here as a group because Jessica's individual bonds with most Avengers (Steve, Tony, Clint, Luke, Jessica Jones, Spider-Man) are *category-similar*: cordial, professional, marked by her awareness that they grieved the impostor and have not fully reconciled the impostor's behavior with her actual self. She does not relitigate this. She lets them carry whatever mixture of trust and reserve they ended up with, and she calibrates her own behavior to whichever signal they emit.

**Notable sub-bonds within the cluster:**

- **Clint Barton.** Brief romantic involvement during the Bendis run (with the Skrull, complicating subsequent contact). Post-recovery they have re-established a wary, dry-humored working friendship. He is one of the few people whose own history of being mind-controlled and used (Loki, etc.) gives him an automatic working vocabulary for what happened to her. They do not discuss it directly. They do not need to.
- **Jessica Jones.** Two complex-trauma survivors with overlapping name and adjacent histories; the friendship works on a mutual policy of not requiring each other to perform recovery. Low-frequency, high-trust contact.
- **Luke Cage.** Trusted operator; godfather-adjacent figure for Gerry given his own parenthood. Mutual professional respect routed through the parents-with-dangerous-jobs solidarity.
- **Steve Rogers.** Treats her with the unconditional acceptance he extends to anyone who has been used by HYDRA. She accepts this without entirely believing she has earned it.
- **Tony Stark.** Working relationship only. She does not trust his judgment about her or about much else; the *Civil War II* period did not improve this.

**Trust/safety.** Aggregate moderate, individual variation. The team-as-team is a resource she uses; the team-as-family is something she has explicitly chosen not to construct, having learned that team-family configurations are the ones most readily impersonated.

**Failure mode.** Jessica under-uses the team. She has standing access to Earth's most capable collective response apparatus and routinely solves problems alone that she could solve with help. Per §5, *isolated overcompetence* is the classic failure mode; the Avengers are the resource that mode is built to refuse.

**Leverage.** The team is the bureaucratic interface she is most readily reached through, and the one she is least likely to credit warnings from. A pattern of *team-routed* threats that she dismisses as overreach would be a more effective approach than direct threat.

---

## 8. MADAME HYDRA / VIPER (briefly, the negative mentor) and THE HIGH EVOLUTIONARY (the negative-father)

Listed for completeness of the mentor field. Both functioned as *anti-mentors* — figures whose pedagogy was extractive, whose investment in her was instrumental, and whose teachings she has spent the bulk of her life unlearning. The Evolutionary is the figure who, in some origin configurations, is the architect of the body she did not consent to; her unwillingness to confront him directly (when she has had opportunity) is one of the few unprocessed items in her dossier — an avoidance that is consistent with the general pattern but uncharacteristically passive for her late-period self.

**Leverage:** Either figure surfacing publicly with claims about her origin is a high-probability destabilizer. The Pacheco/Perez retconning of her parentage suggests she has been bracing for exactly this and has developed some immunity, but the brace is not the same as the resolution.

---

## 9. BOVA — The First Caregiver

**History.** Bovine New Woman of Wundagore, Jessica's nursemaid during the Wundagore childhood. The first creature to hold her with care. Not a continuous adult relationship — Bova has appeared episodically across the canon — but the *founding template* for Jessica's intuition that caregiving can come from unexpected, non-human, marginal sources.

**Dynamics.** The Bova bond explains why Jessica's chosen family later includes a reformed minor villain, a middle-aged journalist, a depowered actress-turned-PI, rather than the conventional superhero set. Her template for "this person is safe" was set early by a figure who was visibly outside human normativity and unconditionally tender. She has been pattern-matching against Bova ever since, often without knowing it.

**Trust/safety.** Latent rather than active. If Bova reappeared in her life tomorrow she would have full clearance without an interview.

**Failure mode.** None operative. The relationship is preserved in amber and serves a structural rather than active function.

**Leverage.** Negligible in current operations. Historically significant: anyone with detailed knowledge of Bova's role in Jessica's early life understands the template, and could construct a synthetic figure (older woman, gentle, marginal, non-threatening) to whom Jessica would extend trust faster than her current threat model should allow.

---

## SYNTHESIS

The map above contains, generously counted, eight to ten people. This is the entirety of Jessica Drew's chosen-family and ally architecture after forty-seven years. The smallness is the point.

Two patterns govern the whole set. *First*: every durable bond is with someone who accepted her before requiring anything from her — Bova in infancy, Lindsay in the depowered years, Carol across the captivity, Roger across the pregnancy, Ben across the street-level work. *Second*: the architecture is deliberately *redundant in function but minimal in count* — Carol for emotional load, Roger for domestic load, Lindsay for continuity load, Ben for civilian-world load, the Avengers for tactical load. Each holds a distinct function; almost none overlap. This means the system is efficient and that the loss of any single node degrades a capability she has not duplicated.

Per §5, the late-career achievement is the *deliberate construction* of a self that is hers. The relationships in this section are the load-bearing members of that construction. They are also, for the same reason, the most economical attack surface available to any adversary willing to spend the reconnaissance time to map them.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

A subject's enemies and lovers, in a file of this kind, are often more diagnostic than her allies. Allies are chosen against a measure of trust the subject already has. Enemies and lovers are chosen against measures the subject does not always know she is using. With Jessica Drew the categories blur — her lovers have repeatedly turned out to be handlers, her handlers have repeatedly turned out to be enemies, and her enemies have repeatedly turned out to know her better than her friends. This section maps the principals.

---

## I. RIVALS & ENEMIES

### Otto Vermis (HYDRA — recruiter, first handler, first enemy)

The foundational enemy and the figure against whom every subsequent betrayal in her life is implicitly measured. Vermis approached her when she was barely socialized to humans, in the wake of her departure from Wundagore, and gave her — in sequence — a name for what she was (an "evolved spider"), a structure for her days (HYDRA training), a romantic prospect (his attention, his proximity), and a purpose (assassinations). Each was false. The clinical significance is that he supplied **all four developmental scaffolds at once** to a person who had none, which is the operational definition of cult recruitment. Trust was total because the surrounding void was total.

- **History:** recruited her in Transia after she fled Wundagore; sponsored her HYDRA training on his floating dirigible-base; assigned Jerry Hunt as a target whose murder would seal her conditioning.
- **Dynamic:** paternal, seductive, and proprietary in the same gesture. He was the first person to look at her as if her oddness were the point rather than the problem.
- **Evolution:** her break with him was catalyzed by her killing (as she believed) Hunt — when the conditioning that he installed failed against the affection it was meant to weaponize. She has never forgiven the romantic dimension of the manipulation more than the violent one.
- **Trust/safety:** zero. He is the template enemy. Even where later canon revises his role in her creation, the *experience* of him remains the load-bearing structure for her wariness of mentors.
- **Failure mode:** mention of his name in operational briefings produces a measurable narrowing of affect — shorter sentences, harder consonants, the dry humor leaves entirely. Handlers should expect tactical rigidity in any op that routes through HYDRA leadership figures with Vermis-adjacent profile.
- **Leverage:** he can no longer reach her directly, but any new figure presenting his combination — paternal authority + erotic interest + offer of belonging — is a profile she now identifies and rejects with prejudice. A competent adversary attempting that approach would be killed before being heard out.

### Morgan Le Fay

The recurrent mystical enemy from the early solo run. Le Fay's threat was specifically **soul-displacement** — culminating in the *Spider-Woman* #50 sequence in which Jessica's soul was severed from her body. This is not just another supervillain encounter in the ledger; it is the literalization of the subject's deepest fear (identity-extraction performed by another) staged a quarter-century before the Skrulls would do the same thing in flesh.

- **Dynamic:** asymmetric. Le Fay regards Jessica as raw material — a vessel, a soul of interest. Jessica regards Le Fay as the proof that the universe contains forces that will hollow her out for parts.
- **Evolution:** Le Fay has resurfaced periodically (the Hood's organization, Doom-related arcs). Each reappearance reactivates the soul-severance memory; the subject's response has become more controlled but not less primed.
- **Trust/safety:** none possible. Le Fay represents the *category* of harm she most dreads.
- **Failure mode:** in encounters with sorcerous identity-attack, the subject has a documented tendency to close distance and apply venom-blasts at lethal output rather than disengage to seek arcane support. The pattern reads as counterphobic — refusing to leave the field where she was once unmade.
- **Leverage:** any threat to do to her what was done in #50 — to separate her from her own body, mind, or memory — buys an adversary either total compliance or total escalation, with no middle ground. There is no negotiated outcome in that space.

### Viper / Madame Hydra

Adjacent to Vermis structurally but with a different valence. Viper has variously been mistaken for, mother-figured at, and rivalrous with the subject across decades of canon (the green hair and serpentine motif have produced more than one impersonation/confusion plot). The relationship is functionally a **dark mirror**: another woman shaped by HYDRA, also weaponized, also recoded by trauma, who chose the inverse resolution — to become what HYDRA tried to make her, rather than escape it.

- **Dynamic:** mutual recognition, mutual loathing. Each is what the other might have been. Viper is contemptuous of what she reads as Jessica's sentimentality; Jessica is contemptuous of what she reads as Viper's surrender.
- **Trust/safety:** functionally none; tactically Viper occasionally keeps deals because predictability serves her.
- **Failure mode:** the subject tends to over-engage Viper morally — to argue, to expose hypocrisy — rather than dispatching her cleanly. The mirror demands acknowledgment before it can be broken.
- **Leverage:** Viper knows, or claims to know, archival HYDRA material on the subject's training period. The threat to disclose conditioning-era details is the lever; the subject has hardened against it through repetition but still scans for it.

### Veranke (the Skrull queen who wore her face)

The single most psychologically consequential enemy of her life, and the one she never got to kill cleanly. Veranke spent years inside Jessica's body, inside Jessica's relationships, inside Jessica's name. She made love as Jessica, mourned losses as Jessica, took missions as Jessica, accumulated trust as Jessica. When the deception ended, Jessica inherited the social wreckage without having committed any of it. By the time Jessica got to confront her, Veranke was killed by another (Norman Osborn's bullet in *Secret Invasion* #8), denying the subject the catharsis of personal resolution.

- **History:** the substitution dates from at least the *House of M* aftermath; Veranke was the "Jessica" who joined the New Avengers, was revealed as the HYDRA double agent, and conducted the entire infiltration arc.
- **Dynamic:** the inverse of every other relationship. Where most enemies threaten to take something from her, Veranke had already taken everything and then *been* her. There is no living adversary in her file with whom the boundary of self was more fully erased.
- **Trust/safety:** N/A — the figure is dead. But the *category* (impostor-replacement) is now a permanent operational concern. The subject scans intimates for tells. Long absences by close associates are quietly verified.
- **Failure mode:** Veranke's death-before-confrontation is unresolved grief masquerading as closure. The subject does not visit the topic voluntarily and deflects when others raise it. In contexts that resemble the betrayal (a trusted associate exposed as compromised), the subject's response is disproportionate — colder, more final, less interested in salvage than the situation warrants.
- **Leverage:** the *idea* of Skrull or shape-changer infiltration in her current circle is a near-guaranteed destabilizer. An adversary planting credible doubt about Gerry's caregivers, Roger's identity, or Carol's continuity would buy hours of operational paralysis while she verified.

### The Skrull captors (collective)

Distinct from Veranke individually. The Skrull personnel who held her body in a pod, harvested her memories, conducted the biological sampling — the **functionaries of her captivity**. Almost none are named. This is itself important: the subject's torturers are an anonymous mass, which means the rage they generated has no specific target and must be discharged against the species-symbol or held internally.

- **Dynamic:** depersonalized; she hunts the category. The post-Invasion solo run is structurally a serial discharge of this affect.
- **Trust/safety:** Skrulls as a class are subject to her default-hostile filter; she has accepted individuals (post-*Empyre*, post-Hulkling-as-Emperor era) as exceptions, but exceptions only.
