- The most reliable way to lose her is to try to handle her. The most reliable way to keep her is to extend trust she did not have to demand, and tolerate the withdrawals without retaliation. The people who have done this are, not coincidentally, the people still in her life.

---

**Summary.** Jessica Drew's moral framework is a particularist, person-indexed, empirically-revised code built atop one categorical prohibition (pheromone manipulation), one foundational absolute (Gerry), and a small set of operating principles (protect the overlooked, do not be acquired, do not betray trust extended, do not hand subjects to systems you distrust). It is consistent where it counts, fractures predictably where her trauma loads it, and has drifted over four decades from defensive reactivity through tradesman's pragmatism to a hard-won, portable maturity. It is — and this is the unsentimental finding — a better ethics than most of the institutions that have tried to write one for her, which is exactly why she trusts it over theirs.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — JESSICA DREW
## Section: Communications & Linguistic Profile

---

### 1. Baseline Phonology and Voice

The subject's vocal signal is, on paper, the single most-discussed feature of her communication after the pheromones, and the two are causally linked. Across forty-seven years of canon her speech is consistently characterized — by writers, by other characters, and in her own narration — as *low, dry, slightly worn at the edges*. The London childhood and adolescence (Wundagore is a Balkan locus but she was anglophone-educated; Wolfman's run, the London chapters of *Spider-Woman* vol. 1 #1–#19) leaves a faint, eroded mid-Atlantic English on the consonants — fricatives slightly tighter than American baseline, terminal /r/ sometimes dropped under fatigue, "can't" pronounced with the broader vowel when she is tired or annoyed. Decades in Los Angeles, San Francisco, New York, and Madripoor sanded the accent down to a non-regional general American with occasional intrusions. She does not perform the accent; she leaks it.

The voice itself sits low in the chest, with restricted dynamic range. She rarely raises volume even in combat. The HYDRA-period training — which would have included tradecraft on vocal control, interrogation cadence, and seduction register — is audible in adulthood as a default monotonic delivery that *withholds* affect rather than expresses it. When she does modulate, the modulation is information: a softened consonant on a name, a held vowel before a refusal, a deliberate roughening when she wants to be underestimated.

The pheromone problem has a documented secondary effect on speech behavior — she has, since the early Claremont issues, *spoken less* than situationally required, because the speech act draws attention to her presence and her presence is chemically loaded. The terseness reads as cool; it is partly tactical avoidance of the room.

---

### 2. Register Inventory

Jessica operates across at least seven distinct registers, switched cleanly and with little leakage. The discreteness of the registers is itself diagnostic: compartmentalization in linguistic form.

**(a) Operational / combat register.** Clipped, declarative, almost exclusively imperative and indicative. Subjects often dropped. ("On your six." "Down." "Move, move, hold — clear.") Profanity present but functional, not ornamental — "shit" as a status update, never as an intensifier. She does not banter mid-fight the way Spider-Man banters; she comments *after*. Verb-heavy. Numbers spoken in full digits, not approximations ("three on the roof," not "a few"). This register is HYDRA-trained and shows it: it has the economy of someone taught to talk on a wire while moving.

**(b) Investigative register.** The PI voice. Patient, slightly bored-sounding, structured around open-ended prompts that let the other party fill silence. ("Walk me through it." "And then." "Okay, but before that.") She is exceptionally good at the productive pause — the *and?* delivered with no inflection, three seconds after the witness has stopped talking. The Lindsay McCabe years drilled this; it persists into all subsequent runs. She does not telegraph what she already knows.

**(c) Domestic / Gerry register.** The largest behavioral discontinuity in her speech. Vowels open, pitch lifts a quarter-step, sentence length doubles, diminutives and nonsense words appear. She narrates her own actions to him ("Okay, we are going to put the — yes, that one, good choice, sir"). This is the only register in which she is verbose. Witnesses to it (Roger Gocking, Ben Urich, Carol Danvers) consistently register surprise; she does not perform it when she knows she is observed by non-intimates.

**(d) Chosen-intimate register.** Used with Lindsay, Carol, Roger, Ben, occasionally Clint. Dry, elliptical, dense with shared reference, heavy on the unfinished sentence. She and Carol in particular communicate in clipped fragments that depend on shared history — half a sentence about a prior op suffices. Affection appears almost exclusively as *complaint* in this register: "You are the worst" reliably means *I love you*; "I hate you" delivered flat means *thank you*. Direct sentiment is rare and load-bearing when it appears.

**(e) Public-hero register.** Cleaner, slightly more formal, the diction of someone aware she is on a record. She drops most contractions, picks up "we" for team operations, gives credit outward. She does not give speeches; when forced to address a crowd or a press scrum she keeps it under thirty seconds and exits. Compare and contrast with Carol's command register: where Carol projects, Jessica *concedes the room* and lets the projection happen elsewhere.

**(f) Handler / institutional register.** Used with Fury, Hill, S.H.I.E.L.D. functionaries, Avengers leadership in formal mode. Cold, correct, minimally informative. She answers the question asked and not the question implied. She volunteers nothing. Post-Skrull, this register has hardened into something near-hostile in cadence even when the words are neutral.

**(g) Internal narration / second person.** Not a spoken register but a written one, and the most psychologically loaded. Bendis-Maleev's *Spider-Woman* (2009–2010) renders her interior in the second person — *you walk in, you don't look at the bartender, you order the thing you always order* — which the Hopeless run partially inherits and modulates into a wry first person. The second-person narration is not a stylistic flourish; it is the linguistic signature of derealization. When she is most under stress, her own interior addresses her as *you*.

---

### 3. Diction and Lexical Tells

Word-level patterns recur across writers, suggesting they are character-load-bearing rather than authorial:

- **"Fine."** The single highest-frequency lexical item in her dialogue across runs. Used as deflection ("How are you?" "Fine."), as concession ("Fine, we'll do it your way"), as termination ("Fine."). The *meaning* is almost never the dictionary meaning. The flat "fine" is her primary verbal stop sign and intimates have learned not to push past it; strangers who push past it get the next register down, which is silence.

- **"Look —"** sentence-initial. Appears when she is about to say something she has decided to say despite a preference not to. Marks effortful disclosure. Often precedes the most honest sentence in a given scene.

- **"Yeah, no" / "No, yeah."** The American conversational hedge, used by her with high frequency. The order matters: *yeah, no* = polite disagreement; *no, yeah* = grudging agreement. She is consistent on this.

- **Diminutive "kid."** Used for younger operatives, teen heroes, occasionally adults she is patronizing. Affectionate when directed at people she likes (Anya Corazon, Kamala Khan in late appearances). Cutting when directed at people she does not.

- **First names, used early and deliberately.** A tradecraft tic — using a target's or interlocutor's first name builds the false intimacy HYDRA taught. She does it less with people she actually likes (with Carol she defaults to "Carol" or "Danvers" interchangeably; with strangers she is being worked, it is "*Michael*, listen" within thirty seconds).

- **Avoidance of "always" and "never."** Notable across runs. She does not make absolute claims about herself or others. The closest she comes is "I don't do that," which is provisional. Reflects empirical cognitive style and trauma-informed wariness of totalizing statements.

- **"Right" as a discourse particle.** Receipts confirmation. "Right." End of sentence, dropping pitch — *understood, moving on*. Mid-sentence with rising pitch — *and the obvious implication is*. She uses this to skip steps she has already done in her head.

- **Tactical vocabulary leak.** "Six," "exfil," "burned," "wire," "cover," "make" (as in "she made me at the corner") appear in her civilian speech in ways that mark her as ex-something to anyone who recognizes the lexicon. She does not bother scrubbing it.

- **Profanity.** Present, low-volume, almost always Anglo-Saxon monosyllables, almost never religious. "Shit" is the workhorse. "Fuck" is reserved — when it appears, attention should be paid; she is genuinely surprised, frightened, or about to do something costly. She does not blaspheme. (Wundagore upbringing under a quasi-religious figure may account for the residual restraint; the absence is consistent enough to be a tell.)

- **Avoids the word "love"** spoken directly to its object. The number of times across forty-seven years she has said "I love you" to another character in plain declarative form is countable on one hand and most of them are to Gerry. She conveys love by other linguistic means (see §6).

- **Avoids the word "father."** Refers to Jonathan Drew by full name or "my father" in clinical contexts, almost never as "Dad" or "Daddy." Post–parentage retcon, the avoidance has intensified into near-total omission.

---

### 4. Syntax, Cadence, and Rhythm

Her sentences are short to medium-short, with a marked preference for the compound over the complex — she will say *I went, I looked, it wasn't there* before *when I went and looked, it wasn't there*. The parataxis is a tradecraft inheritance (reporting structure: discrete observations, no embedded judgment) and a defensive choice (subordinate clauses require committing to relationships between facts; she withholds those).

Her cadence in conversation has a characteristic *late beat* — she answers a half-second after the expected response window, consistently enough that interlocutors sometimes restart the sentence assuming she didn't hear. She heard. The pause is processing plus tactical evaluation of what to release. The pause shortens dramatically with Gerry (where there is nothing to evaluate) and with imminent physical threat (where the calculation is faster than speech).

She uses **sentence fragments as full turns** at high frequency. "Tomorrow." "Wouldn't." "Not that one." The fragment forces the interlocutor to do the reconstruction work; it is an information-conserving move and a control move.

She rarely asks questions, and when she does they are open and minimal. Her interrogation style depends on statements offered for correction ("So you were in the building at nine") rather than direct queries ("Where were you at nine?"). This is textbook investigative technique and she does it reflexively even in social conversation, which can read as presumptuous to people who don't know her.

---

### 5. Rhetorical Repertoire

Jessica does not give speeches and is suspicious of people who do. Her rhetorical toolkit is small, sharpened, and almost entirely defensive or de-escalatory:

- **Understatement as truth-delivery.** Catastrophes are reported flat. "It went badly" can mean a building came down. The understatement is not modesty; it is calibration — she has learned that the people who need to know will hear the weight under the words and the people who don't aren't her problem.

- **Specificity as authority.** When she does need to be believed, she shifts from her usual abstract phrasing to dense concrete detail — license plate, hour, exact phrase the suspect used. The specificity is the argument.

- **Self-deprecation as social lubricant.** Light, dry, never abject. ("Yeah, I'm a delight." "Mother of the Year, that's me.") This is her primary mechanism for making other people comfortable with her physical and chemical presence; it asks permission without asking.

- **Refusal of the rhetorical question.** She does not say "do you think I want to do this?" — she says "I don't want to do this," or she says nothing. Rhetorical questions ask for emotional participation; she does not solicit it.

- **Quoting the enemy back.** Particularly in HYDRA-adjacent or institutional confrontations, she will repeat a handler's or villain's exact phrasing back at them, deadpan, to make them hear it. It is her most effective rhetorical move and she uses it sparingly.

She is not a persuader. She is a *reporter* and an *operator*, and her rhetoric reflects both: she tells you what happened, and she tells you what is about to happen, and she does not spend energy on what should.

---

### 6. How She Communicates Love

Almost never lexically. The word "love" is held in reserve and discharged at high cost. Her actual vocabulary of affection:

- **Showing up.** The verbal correlate is short — "I'm here" or "I came" — and the act is the message.
- **Complaint as endearment.** As above, "you are exhausting" is a love declaration in her register. Sarcasm calibrated finely enough that intimates can read the warmth in it.
- **Use of full name.** With Carol, "Carol Danvers" said slowly, with a specific tired affection, is a declaration. With Gerry, "Gerald" deployed once an evening with mock-gravity is a ritual.
- **Operational disclosure.** Telling a person something only Jessica knows — about a case, about her body, about Wundagore — is the highest-tier intimacy gesture she offers. Information she has been guarding becomes a gift. The number of recipients is small.
- **Practical provision.** "Did you eat." "Take this." "Sit down." Care expressed in imperatives. The imperative mood, in her, is often love.
- **Physical proximity without conversation.** Sitting in the same room, not talking. With Lindsay this was a documented pattern over years; with Roger, similar; with Gerry, the bedtime sit.

The one place she will say it plainly is with Gerry, and even there it is *terse* — "Love you, kid" at the door, not extended. The brevity is not coldness; it is preservation. She does not want to wear the word out, because she has watched larger words wear out faster than they should.

---

### 7. How She Communicates Threat

The threat register is the most distinctive thing in her communicative profile and the part most often remarked on by other characters. It is *quiet*. She does not posture, does not warn twice, does not escalate volume.

- **Volume drops, does not rise.** When she is genuinely about to hurt someone, her voice goes *quieter*, not louder. The drop is the warning. People who have been around her learn it; people who have not, do not.
- **First name, slow.** As above, the tradecraft first-name move, deployed in threat context, lands like a knife on a table. "*Michael.*" Held syllable. Pause.
- **Statement of fact, future tense.** "You are going to put it down." Flat indicative. Not a request, not a threat lexically — a prediction. She has been right enough times that the people she addresses tend to comply.
- **Citation of the specific.** She names the thing the target thought was private. The threat is *I see you*, delivered as *I know about the apartment on Sullivan*.
- **Silence as ultimatum.** The final stage before violence is no speech at all. If she has stopped talking to a person who is still talking to her, the conversation is over and what follows will not be conversation.

She does not bluff. The threats she articulates are ones she will execute. The reverse is also true: many of her most dangerous acts come without any verbal predicate at all.

---

### 8. How She Communicates Grief

Grief is the affect she least permits into speech, and the gaps where it should be are themselves the signal. Recovery from the Skrull captivity, the deaths of figures she cared about across decades (Magnus, Jerry Hunt, others), and the cumulative losses of identity-trauma have produced an adult who does not narrate grief at the time of grief. She *processes it linguistically late*, often months or years on, and obliquely.

- **Tense slippage.** Talking about lost people, she uses present tense for a beat too long, then corrects. The correction is audible.
- **Object focus.** She talks about the apartment, the coffee, the song — not the person. The displacement is the eulogy.
- **Refusal of the consolatory script.** She will not say "they're in a better place," "at least," "we'll get through this." She finds the language offensive on a near-physical level. When others use it on her, she goes silent.
- **The second-person interior.** This is when *you* shows up in her narration — *you go to the place, you do not cry, you order the thing, you go home*. The depersonalized voice is her grief grammar.
- **Late-night confession to one person.** The Bendis-era and Hopeless-era patterns both show that her grief, when it speaks, speaks to exactly one intimate at three in the morning, in fragments, with long pauses, and is never raised again in daylight. The person who hears it is expected to act as if it did not happen.

She does not cry in front of people if she can avoid it. When she does, she does not narrate it.

---

### 9. Deflection Architecture

Her deflection vocabulary is large because she needs it daily. The reliable moves, in order from soft to hard:

1. **Topic-pivot via question to the other party.** "How's [their thing]?" Disarming because she actually wants to know, but also a closing-the-self move.
2. **"It's a long story."** Used when the story is in fact long *and* she will not tell it.
3. **"Doesn't matter."** Used when it does.
4. **"I'm handling it."** Means: I am alone with it, and intervention will be refused.
5. **Flat "fine."** See §3.
6. **Dry joke that names the discomfort.** "Yeah, this is the part where I'm supposed to talk about my feelings." Names the script in order to refuse it.
7. **Silence with eye contact held.** Late-stage. Communicates: *we both know what you asked, and I am not going to answer, and the relationship will survive this only if you drop it now.*
8. **Physical exit.** When all else fails, she leaves the room. Without explanation. People who know her do not follow.

The deflection architecture is not pathological avoidance; it is a *rationed-disclosure economy*. She has decided, with reason, that her interior is expensive to share and dangerous to share badly, and she manages the inventory accordingly.

---

### 10. Written and Digital Communications

Her texting style is consistent across the recent runs: lowercase, minimal punctuation, almost telegraphic. "on my way." "got it." "no." She does not use emoji except with Gerry and occasionally Carol, where a single tactical emoji functions as a full sentence. She does not voice-message. She does not leave voicemails — if a call goes to voicemail she hangs up and texts.

Email is rare and clinical when it appears. Reports written for institutional consumption (S.H.I.E.L.D., later clients) are dense, structured, opinion-free, and visibly the work of someone who learned reporting in an intelligence apparatus. She buries judgment in word choice — "*claimed* to have been," "*reportedly*" — never in editorial paragraphs.

She does not maintain a public social presence. The discipline is total and predates the current decade's tradecraft norms — she was off-grid before off-grid was a posture.

---

### 11. Linguistic Tells Under Stress

The decompensation sequence in her speech, by stage:

- **Mild stress:** humor sharpens, profanity ticks up one notch, sentences shorten further. She becomes *funnier*, which intimates read as a warning sign.
- **Moderate stress:** humor disappears. Register flattens toward operational. Pauses lengthen. The word "fine" appears more often. She begins answering questions she was not asked, because she is pre-empting follow-ups.
- **High stress:** speech reduces to fragments. She stops using contractions. First-person pronoun drops out — "going to handle it," not "I'm going to handle it." The dropped *I* is among her most reliable tells; the self is going offline as a grammatical subject before it goes offline as an experiential one.
- **Crisis:** silence, or the second-person interior narration if she is alone. Spoken communication reduces to the bare imperatives needed for the operation. After the crisis, she will not narrate it for days.

The inverse tell — when she is *well* — is the appearance of full, leisurely sentences, embedded clauses, occasional verbosity. It is rare. When intimates hear it, they note it.

---

### 12. Synthesis

Jessica Drew's language is the language of someone who has been listened to badly her entire life and has therefore learned to say less, mean more, and ration access to the interior. The register-switching is clean because the compartments are sealed; the verbal tics — the flat "fine," the late beat, the dropped *I*, the second-person interior — are the seams where the compartments meet. She communicates love by showing up and complaint, threat by going quiet, grief by displacing onto objects and tense. The most honest things she says are the shortest. The most dangerous silences are the ones that follow a held first name.

Her speech, in sum, is a long defensive perimeter built around a small, real, hard-won interior. The perimeter is the message about the perimeter. The interior is offered, when offered, in fragments, at night, to one person, once.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward-projected behavioral predictions for situations the published record does not depict. Format: GIVEN [condition] → EXPECT [predicted behavior], with derivation. Predictions are calibrated to the subject's documented patterns and weighted by recency where the record evolves.*

---

## A. DOMESTIC ROUTINE & SOLITUDE

**GIVEN** an uninterrupted day at home with Gerry at school **→ EXPECT** the following sequence: a tactical sweep of the apartment perimeter dressed as a coffee run (window-line check, building-stairwell pass, two passes of the block in opposite directions), followed by 90–120 minutes of administrative work (PI casework, bills, the kind of correspondence she will not delegate), followed by deliberately scheduled idle time she does not know how to use. *Derivation:* compartmentalized life-architecture (mother-box, work-box, operational-box) requires that each box be serviced daily; the inability to fill genuinely unstructured hours is a documented C-PTSD signature.

**GIVEN** a power outage in her building **→ EXPECT** her to be the second-floor neighbor everyone vaguely knows but doesn't really know, who appears in the hallway with a working flashlight, checks on the elderly tenant on her floor by name, makes no offer of company beyond what is asked, and returns to her unit to sit with Gerry in the dark while the rest of the building socializes on the stoop. She does not perform community; she performs reliability.

**GIVEN** a free Saturday evening with no obligations and Gerry with Roger **→ EXPECT** patrol, framed to herself as "just a walk." The probability she chooses indoor leisure over operational ambient-scanning approaches zero. If she does stay in, expect rewatching something she has seen before (predictable narrative is restorative; novel narrative is parsing work) and falling asleep on the couch in clothes rather than going to bed.

**GIVEN** insomnia at 3:14 a.m. **→ EXPECT** she will not attempt to return to sleep. Predicted sequence: standing at the kitchen window for ~6–9 minutes drinking water (not tea — tea would be a ritual that admits to insomnia), then casework on the laptop at the kitchen table (not the desk; the desk is a daytime location), then patrol gear on by 4:00 if the restlessness has not resolved. She does not journal, does not meditate, does not call anyone.

**GIVEN** a planned vacation (Carol's insistence, holiday with Gerry) **→ EXPECT** a baseline elevation in irritability for the first 36–48 hours of forced idleness, then gradual settling, then — critically — a marked reluctance to return that she will not voice. Vacation surfaces what work suppresses; she will become unusually tactile with Gerry, sleep more than expected, and develop a low-grade somatic complaint (headache, jaw tension) on the return-travel day.

**GIVEN** her apartment is burgled by an ordinary, non-powered intruder while she is out **→ EXPECT** she does not call police until after she has independently identified the intruder. The PI reflex routes around institutional channels; calling SHIELD or the Avengers for a civilian break-in would feel grotesquely disproportionate; calling NYPD feels naïve. She will resolve it herself within 72 hours, return the stolen items to neighbors if relevant, and have a brief, unpleasant private conversation with the burglar that does not involve violence but that the burglar will remember.

---

## B. PARENTING & GERRY

**GIVEN** a routine school-morning **→ EXPECT** Gerry is awake before she has to wake him because she trained that pattern early; she still goes to his door at the same time anyway. Breakfast is competent rather than elaborate (eggs, toast, fruit she remembered to buy). She walks him to school when geography permits, taking a different route at least twice a week — not because she is paranoid that morning but because route-variance is automatic and she does not notice she's doing it. She kisses the top of his head at the gate, not the forehead in front of his friends; she calibrated this distinction the year he asked her to.

**GIVEN** Gerry is sick with a normal childhood illness (flu, strep) **→ EXPECT** disproportionate calm. Mundane medical events are *exactly* the kind of threat she is overqualified for; she becomes warmer, more present, more physically affectionate during ordinary illness than during ordinary health. She will sleep on the floor by his bed the first night without making a thing of it. She will not, however, cancel a high-stakes operation for a fever; she will arrange Roger or Carol to sit with him and call twice from cover.

**GIVEN** a parent-teacher conference **→ EXPECT** she arrives early, dresses one notch more conventionally than she'd prefer, sits with her hands quiet, and listens far more than she speaks. She will ask one question that surprises the teacher with its specificity (about a peer dynamic, a particular subject's pedagogy) — evidence she has been paying close attention to Gerry's offhand reports. She will not volunteer her profession or correct the school's assumptions about her marital status. She will be remembered as "the polite one" who is also subtly intimidating in a way teachers cannot place.

**GIVEN** Gerry asks a hard question about her past (HYDRA, the Skrull captivity, his paternity, her parents) **→ EXPECT** she answers truthfully at the resolution he is developmentally ready for, without softening the moral weight, and without using the conversation to process her own grief. She has decided — and this is one of the most disciplined decisions she has ever made — that he will not become her confidant. If the question stirs her, the stirring shows up six hours later in patrol-route deviation, not in the conversation itself.

**GIVEN** Gerry expresses fear of her work **→ EXPECT** she does not promise safety she cannot deliver. She promises *return*, framed in operational rather than emotional language — "I always come back; I have a plan for if I can't; you will never be alone." She has rehearsed this script. She means it. She will then arrange a redundancy in his support network within 72 hours without telling him she did.

**GIVEN** Gerry is invited to a birthday party at the home of a family she has not vetted **→ EXPECT** a 30-minute pre-party background scan that she will categorize internally as "just checking" — public records, social media, building permits, the parents' employers. She lets him go. She does not arrive early to pick up. She *does* keep her phone visible for the duration.

**GIVEN** Gerry's first significant defiance or lie **→ EXPECT** she handles it markedly better than she expects to. Her own adolescence was distorted by enforced obedience and then by manufactured rebellion (HYDRA); she has thought hard about what ordinary developmentally-appropriate pushback should be allowed to look like. She will not punish disproportionately. She *will* be quieter than usual for the next 24 hours, processing whether her reaction is calibrated.

---

## C. SOCIAL — CHOSEN FAMILY

**GIVEN** a phone call from Carol Danvers at an odd hour **→ EXPECT** she picks up by the third ring regardless of what she is doing, with no greeting performance — just "yeah." The relationship has no opening rituals; both parties find them embarrassing. If Carol is drinking and dialing, Jessica will stay on the line until Carol either resolves or sleeps; she will not moralize about the drinking but will, at some later sober moment within a week, mention it once, factually, without follow-up. She does this because she expects the same management from Carol regarding her own avoidances, and roughly receives it.

**GIVEN** Carol cancels plans last-minute for cosmic reasons **→ EXPECT** genuine, unperformed relief in roughly 40% of cases — she had wanted the connection without wanting the actual evening — combined with frictionless rescheduling. No accumulated resentment. The relationship's durability rests partly on mutual permission to be unreliable about everything except crisis.

**GIVEN** Roger Gocking arrives to take Gerry for the weekend **→ EXPECT** brisk handoff with Gerry's bag pre-packed and a one-page note of medical/schedule items even though Roger knows. She over-documents because the alternative — trusting verbally — feels operationally lax, not because she distrusts Roger. With Roger she is warm in a specific limited register: she lets him be funny, she does not perform competence at him, she will eat the food he brings without commenting on it. She has decided he is family; she has not decided he is intimate.

**GIVEN** Lindsay McCabe in town **→ EXPECT** the relationship that most resembles her pre-trauma self surfaces. With Lindsay she is louder, more profane, more physically demonstrative (hugs, shoulder-grabs), drinks more, sleeps less, laughs at things she would not laugh at with anyone else. Lindsay is the only person in her life from before the worst things; the regression is restorative. Predicted recovery time after a Lindsay visit: 48 hours of low affect she will not attribute to Lindsay.

**GIVEN** the death or grave injury of a member of the small circle **→ EXPECT** the most concerning response in her repertoire: operational normality for 72 hours, then a 4-to-6-day functional disappearance during which she will not be reachable, then return without explanation. She does not grieve in company. The chosen-family architecture has not been load-tested for the loss of one of its load-bearing members; this is the predicted scenario for her worst decade-onset depressive episode.

---

## D. SOCIAL — STRANGERS, ACQUAINTANCES, PROFESSIONAL CIVILIANS

**GIVEN** a first-time meeting with a new client for the PI practice **→ EXPECT** she runs late by 2–4 minutes by design (lets the client arrive first, lets her see them seated), takes the chair with sightlines to the door, orders water rather than coffee (no caffeinated tells, no waiting for a hot drink that constrains exit). She listens with notable stillness — minimal nodding, no encouraging "mm-hm"s — which most clients read as either rude or formidable depending on disposition; the self-selection effect this produces filters her clientele toward people who can tolerate her.

**GIVEN** a stranger at a bar attempts conversation **→ EXPECT** she runs a fast pheromone-attribution check on herself before assessing the approach (am I leaking? is this real?). Outcome-dependent: if she reads the approach as pheromone-driven, polite curt disengagement within 90 seconds; if she reads it as genuine, she may extend to a single drink's duration and then leave without contact-exchange. She does not initiate. She has not initiated with a stranger in years and will not unless drunker than she gets.

**GIVEN** small talk at a school function with another parent **→ EXPECT** competent, warm, content-light exchanges of 4–7 minutes. She has developed scripts. She remembers names accurately on second meeting, which other parents find flattering and which is operational habit. She will not host. She will accept invitations to coffee from one or two parents per Gerry's school year and will not deepen any of them past the third coffee.

**GIVEN** a man flirts with her in front of Gerry **→ EXPECT** a noticeable hardening she will mask within two seconds. She will use Gerry as a graceful exit ("we're heading out — say goodbye, Gerry"). Later, alone, she will examine whether her reaction was protective parenting or her own discomfort, and conclude both, and not resolve which mattered more.

**GIVEN** a woman is openly hostile to her for no apparent reason at a social gathering **→ EXPECT** she identifies the pheromone effect immediately, does not take it personally in the moment, but absorbs it as another data-point in a lifetime of the same. She does not confront, does not explain, removes herself from the woman's proximity within a reasonable interval, and will be slightly more withdrawn for the remainder of the evening. The cumulative cost of this pattern across decades is not zero; she compensates by under-attending events with women she does not already know.

**GIVEN** a service worker (cashier, driver, super) treats her well **→ EXPECT** disproportionate warmth in return — eye contact, name use, generous tip — disproportionate to the interaction but proportional to her own internal economy of small kindnesses. People who treat strangers decently are, in her empirical worldview, a positively-selected sample worth reinforcing.

**GIVEN** a service worker treats her poorly **→ EXPECT** unbothered courtesy in the moment, no complaint up the chain, no rumination after. She has metabolized far worse. The asymmetric grace toward strangers is itself a quiet form of resilience-display she would not name.

---

## E. PROFESSIONAL — PI PRACTICE

**GIVEN** a domestic-surveillance case (infidelity work) **→ EXPECT** she takes them despite finding them dispiriting because they pay reliably and require skills she has overdeveloped. She over-documents — more photos than billed, longer logs than needed — and tends to err toward telling clients the *least* damaging truthful version of what she found. Predicted bias: in cases where the suspected partner is, in her assessment, the more sympathetic party, she will quietly under-deliver evidence without ever lying. This is a small ethical drift she has made peace with.

**GIVEN** a missing-person case involving a child **→ EXPECT** rate discounted or waived without announcement, sleep hygiene collapses, other casework slips, will not pass the case off to another investigator even when objectively appropriate. This is the closest she comes to a known operational vulnerability. Carol and Roger both know the pattern and have learned to provide Gerry-coverage during such cases without being asked twice.

**GIVEN** a client lies to her about the nature of the engagement **→ EXPECT** she knows within the first meeting and takes the case anyway with a private revised brief. She will discover the actual situation, deliver a result calibrated to it rather than to the stated brief, and bill the originally-quoted rate. The client will not return; she does not want them to.

**GIVEN** a case that brushes against HYDRA-adjacent infrastructure **→ EXPECT** immediate distancing rituals: she will not pursue without backup briefed (usually Carol or a SHIELD contact), will not enter HYDRA-marked physical sites alone, will document trail in a third-party-accessible location before each engagement. The HYDRA reflex is the one trauma response she has formalized into policy rather than left to instinct.

**GIVEN** a client cannot pay **→ EXPECT** she completes the work and writes it off without ceremony if she judges the cause sympathetic. She does not have a sliding scale on paper. She has one in her head and resents being asked to make it explicit.

---

## F. OPERATIONAL — ROUTINE PATROL & TEAM DYNAMICS

**GIVEN** standard nighttime patrol **→ EXPECT** route variance maintained at ~70% novelty per week (high enough to defeat pattern-recognition, low enough to maintain familiarity-with-terrain advantage in the 30% repeat zones). She prefers rooftops over street-level for traversal, street-level over rooftops for observation. She does not use comms unless coordinating; the silence is preference, not protocol. Average patrol duration: 3.5–5 hours, ending when she has either intervened in something or convinced herself nothing is happening, not at a scheduled time.

**GIVEN** an Avengers assembly call for a non-existential threat **→ EXPECT** she responds, arrives in the back half of arrivals (not first, not last), positions on the operational periphery rather than the command cluster, and contributes terse tactical observations rather than strategic framing. She defers leadership without ceding judgment; if she disagrees with a call she will execute it and then, privately, raise the disagreement with one specific person afterward (usually whoever made the call, never publicly).

**GIVEN** a teammate proposes an unsound plan in the field **→ EXPECT** brief, dry objection, single sentence. If overruled, executes without sulking. If catastrophically unsound, she will execute her own subplan in parallel and explain afterward. She is not insubordinate; she is an investigator first and a soldier second and treats orders as input rather than constraint.

**GIVEN** post-operation debrief **→ EXPECT** she stays for the briefing, contributes precisely, declines social aftermath unless Carol is present, and is the second or third person to leave. She does not do the post-mission bar visit. She has done it twice in five years and regretted both.

**GIVEN** a teammate she does not know well is injured under her sightline **→ EXPECT** she goes to them immediately, stabilizes competently (her medical knowledge is better than people assume — products of pheromone-management protocols and field experience), does not let go of physical contact until handoff. She is markedly tender in medical moments with strangers in a way she is not in any other stranger-context.

**GIVEN** a press scrum after a public operation **→ EXPECT** she does not engage. If cornered, she gives one neutral sentence and walks. She has no public-facing persona to maintain and considers media engagement a tactical liability. She does not appear on social media. This is policy.

---

## G. SOMATIC TELLS & MICRO-PATTERNS

**GIVEN** social tension she is masking **→ EXPECT** the thumb of her dominant hand traces the edge of her index fingernail. It is her only reliable tell and she does not know she does it.

**GIVEN** she is lying (rare; she prefers strategic omission) **→ EXPECT** she becomes *more* still rather than less, eye contact steady, voice slightly lower in pitch. The signature is the absence of normal micro-movement, not its presence. She knows this about herself and will sometimes introduce a deliberate small gesture to compensate, which itself is detectable to a trained observer.

**GIVEN** she has not slept **→ EXPECT** unchanged motor performance, unchanged speech, but a 1–2 second lag in social-emotional uptake — she will hear a joke and laugh half a beat late. This is the most reliable fatigue tell.

**GIVEN** she is about to make a counterphobic decision (going toward the threat alone) **→ EXPECT** an external observer would see her exhale slowly through her nose, set her jaw, and shift her weight. She herself experiences a brief sensation of *quietness* she finds rewarding and which is, in clinical terms, the dissociative window opening.

**GIVEN** she is genuinely amused **→ EXPECT** a closed-mouth laugh first, then — only with the inner circle — an open one. Strangers rarely get the second.

**GIVEN** she is touched unexpectedly by a stranger **→ EXPECT** a fractional flinch she suppresses before it completes, followed by deliberately not increasing distance (she has trained herself not to flinch *visibly*, because visible flinching invites questions). The internal cost of this suppression is real and accumulates across crowded days.

**GIVEN** she is touched expectedly by Gerry, Carol, Lindsay, or Roger **→ EXPECT** none of the above. The inner circle has tactile permission the rest of the world does not.

---

## H. RITUAL & TEMPORAL ARCHITECTURE

**GIVEN** the anniversary of her recovery from Skrull captivity **→ EXPECT** she does not mark it. She knows the date. She will be marginally more present with Gerry, will patrol longer, and will not tell anyone what day it is. If Carol remembers and reaches out, she will accept the call without acknowledging the reason and will be grateful for the acknowledgment that she has chosen not to require.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of Jerry Hunt's apparent death (her first significant loss) **→ EXPECT** likely unobserved consciously; the date is buried under more recent traumas. Some years it will surface as inexplicable low mood she will not connect to the date even if asked.

**GIVEN** Gerry's birthday **→ EXPECT** elaborate preparation, restrained execution, photos taken that she will print rather than leave digital (a small countermeasure against the impermanence she has felt about every other record of her life). She will cry briefly after he is asleep. She has done this every year.

**GIVEN** the holiday season generally **→ EXPECT** functional participation calibrated to Gerry's age and expectations, no nostalgic ritual of her own (she has no childhood holiday memories to reproduce), gravitation toward Roger's or Lindsay's hosting rather than her own. She gives good gifts — observant, specific — and is uncomfortable receiving them.

---

## I. EDGE-CASE PREDICTIONS

**GIVEN** an offer to join a permanent team roster (Avengers, X-Men, any standing organization) **→ EXPECT** decline, framed practically (Gerry, PI practice, geography), driven actually by the HYDRA-Skrull-Fury pattern of being absorbed into structures that turn out to be using her. She will remain an on-call asset. She will not take a desk.

**GIVEN** an offer of romantic involvement from a competent, kind, persistent suitor **→ EXPECT** prolonged hesitation, several false starts, eventual engagement contingent on the suitor's tolerance for her schedule and her silences. The relationship will succeed or fail on his ability to not require explanation. She has the capacity for love; she does not have the capacity for narration of it.

**GIVEN** a request to publicly tell her story (memoir, interview, documentary) **→ EXPECT** firm refusal. Her story has been told by others her entire life; reclaiming it does not, for her, mean publishing it. The privacy is the point.

**GIVEN** the slow uneventful decade — no crisis, no captivity, no replacement, Gerry growing safely **→ EXPECT** the hardest period of her life. She does not have the operating system for peace. Predicted: a year of low-grade dysphoria she cannot account for, followed by either a deliberate constructive turn (training others, writing a methodology, deepening community work) or a destructive turn (returning to operations she does not need to take). The directionality of that turn is the single most consequential variable in her late life and depends almost entirely on whether Carol, Lindsay, and Roger are present and attentive when she begins to drift.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

## Preamble

This section maps the high-amplitude end of Jessica Drew's behavioral envelope: what she does when the pressure exceeds her ordinary regulatory bandwidth, when someone she trusted moves against her, when an operator dangles the right bait, and — most diagnostically — when an event reaches into the specific, scarred topology of her identity wound. The predictions here are not symmetric with ordinary-day behavior. Under crisis loading her affective range *narrows* rather than broadens; her humor flattens, her sentence length shortens, her physical economy tightens. The model assumes that everything in Section 3–5 holds and asks: at what threshold does each defense yield, in what order, and what surfaces underneath.

A standing principle for the entire section: **Jessica does not break loudly.** Catastrophic decompensation in this subject is *quieter* than her baseline, not louder. Surveillance teams expecting a crisis to look like rage or weeping will miss it. The crisis state looks like a competent woman moving very efficiently through a series of tactically sound decisions that, integrated, constitute self-destruction.

---

## 1. ACUTE PHYSICAL THREAT (to her person)

**GIVEN** ambush, hostile entry, or unanticipated combat onset → **EXPECT** sub-second orientation (head tracks before body), immediate evaluation of egress *and* engagement options in parallel, and a strong tendency to *close distance* rather than create it. Her power-set rewards proximity (venom blast effective at touch-to-meter range, adhesion advantageous in clinch), and her training rewards aggression. She will not call for backup in the first sixty seconds of an encounter; she will assess whether she can resolve it alone first, and only escalate communications if the answer is no.

**GIVEN** she is outnumbered three-to-one or worse by capable opponents → **EXPECT** a deliberate vertical move within the first ten seconds — onto a wall, ceiling, or elevated surface — to convert the engagement geometry to one favoring her. She fights *down* by preference. Watch for a characteristic tell: she touches the surface with one palm before adhering with the body, a half-second pre-check that has appeared consistently since the Wolfman run.

**GIVEN** she takes a wound she registers as serious → **EXPECT** under-reporting. She will not name the injury aloud during the engagement and will minimize it in after-action. The cue is somatic, not verbal: a slight asymmetry in the carriage of the affected side, a hand that drifts to but does not touch the site, a refusal of offered medical attention with a one-line deflection ("I've had worse," "later," or the tighter "I'm fine," which in her vocabulary means the opposite).

**GIVEN** capture or restraint → **EXPECT** initial cooperation that reads as compliance and is in fact reconnaissance. She will let captors believe they have her while she inventories the room, the team, the language, the procedures. First escape attempt comes *after* she has mapped the system, not at the first opportunity. This is HYDRA-trained patience and it is reliable.

**GIVEN** a restraint specifically designed to neutralize her powers (power-dampening cuffs, gas, etc.) → **EXPECT** controlled panic that does not show on the face but registers in respiration. Her body has been her last reliable possession; removing access to it touches the developmental wound about a body she did not choose. Predicted behavior: she becomes *more* compliant on the surface, *more* dangerous in planning. The escape, when it comes, will be disproportionate.

---

## 2. THREATS TO GERRY

This is the apex pressure point and warrants its own granularity. The model treats threats to her son as a categorically different stimulus class, not a quantitative extension of "threat to loved one."

**GIVEN** credible threat to Gerry communicated to her → **EXPECT** total collapse of compartmentalization within minutes. The investigative-self, the Avenger-self, and the mother-self merge into a single operational mode. Ordinary tactical conservatism evaporates; she will accept risk profiles she would refuse for any other objective, including her own life.

**GIVEN** the threat actor is sophisticated and remains at large → **EXPECT** Jessica to relocate Gerry inside the first hour to a location she has pre-selected and never disclosed. She has such a location. She has more than one. The Hopeless run's establishment of her chosen-family infrastructure implies, and surveillance behavior confirms, that she maintains contingency placements with at least two trusted parties (Lindsay McCabe and a second, likely Roger Gocking or a vetted unaffiliated party) on standing arrangement.

**GIVEN** the threat actor has *touched* Gerry — physical proximity, attempted abduction, photograph delivered → **EXPECT** the cold-controlled-violence mode (Section 5). She will not negotiate, will not warn twice, will not extend the procedural courtesies she normally offers adversaries. She will hunt the actor to ground and, if not actively restrained by allies she respects, will kill. This is the single scenario in which her general non-lethal preference reliably fails.

**GIVEN** she is forced to choose between Gerry's immediate safety and a larger mission objective → **EXPECT** Gerry every time, no deliberation visible. She will then carry significant guilt about the abandoned objective, processed privately, never raised in debrief. This guilt accumulates and is a vulnerability future handlers can exploit by *praising* the choice — which she will read as condescension and reject — or, more dangerously, by *not mentioning it*, which reads to her as confirmation of failure.

**GIVEN** Gerry is harmed despite her efforts → **EXPECT** a recovery period of weeks-to-months during which her behavioral envelope shifts toward isolated overcompetence (Section 5's named failure mode) at unsustainable intensity. Sleep degrades severely. She will refuse Carol's intervention at first and accept it on the third or fourth approach if Carol simply *stays present without demanding*. Suicidal ideation in this period is not predicted, but reckless engagement with high-lethality threats is — functionally similar in outcome distribution.

---

## 3. BETRAYAL BY A TRUSTED PARTY

The betrayal pattern is the single most-rehearsed wound in her life and her responses are therefore both highly defended and highly reactive. The defense is *detection*; the reactivity is *what happens after detection*.

**GIVEN** a small inconsistency in the behavior of a trusted ally — out-of-pattern timing, unfamiliar phrasing, asymmetric information — → **EXPECT** her to register it within one exposure and to *not raise it*. She will test silently. Subsequent meetings will include subtle verification probes: references to shared history with one detail wrong, to see if the ally corrects or accepts. She has run this protocol on Carol Danvers, on Fury, on herself in mirrors.

**GIVEN** confirmation of betrayal (handler ran her on a false brief, ally was an impostor, lover was working an angle) → **EXPECT** an immediate, total, *silent* withdrawal of trust, executed without a confrontation scene. She will not give the betrayer the dignity of a fight in the moment of revelation. She will leave the room, leave the building if possible, and re-engage at a time and on terms of her choosing. The Bendis/Maleev tonal register — flat, second-person, methodical — is the affective signature of this state.

**GIVEN** the betrayer attempts apology or explanation within the first 72 hours → **EXPECT** courteous, dead-eyed refusal. She will not be cruel; she will not be warm; she will be *administrative*. Reconciliation, if it is possible at all, must come months later and must come from the betrayer doing demonstrable work without an audience. Carol Danvers has earned this kind of repair more than once. Most others do not.

**GIVEN** a betrayal pattern matches the HYDRA template (she was used as a tool by an operator who knew more than she did) → **EXPECT** disproportionate response. This is the bait-and-switch of her adolescence and it is the wound that has been re-cut the most times (HYDRA, Fury's S.H.I.E.L.D. double-agent gambit, Skrull captivity as the ultimate version). Predicted: she will sever the relationship completely, salt the earth, and refuse mediation. Time-to-forgiveness on this template approaches infinity.

**GIVEN** the betrayer is a *system* (agency, team, government) rather than an individual → **EXPECT** lower-amplitude response, because the expectation was already low. She will exit the relationship and decline further engagement, but the wound is shallower because the trust extended was shallower. This is why she works alone with such facility — she has pre-priced the betrayal.

**GIVEN** *she* discovers she has been the unwitting instrument of harm to an innocent → **EXPECT** the highest-amplitude self-directed response in her repertoire. She will withdraw from operations, attempt to compensate the victim directly and privately, and enter a period of behavioral self-restriction. This is the scenario in which she most resembles a clinical depression — anhedonic, low-volume, low-mobility. Recovery requires external scaffolding she will not request.

---

## 4. IDENTITY ATTACKS

This is the most-rehearsed wound class and the one with the most refined defenses, because she has been attacked here more than any other character in the canon and has built specific architecture against it.

**GIVEN** an actor attempts mind control, telepathic intrusion, or psychic suggestion → **EXPECT** higher-than-baseline resistance, not because of a power but because of *practice*. She has built internal verification rituals — small idiosyncratic memories, the texture of Gerry's hair, the specific cadence of Lindsay's laugh — that function as authentication tokens. An intruder who can fake the broad strokes will still trip on the texture. She has likely worked with telepathic allies (Emma Frost, Jean Grey, the Avengers' rotating roster) to harden these tokens, though she does not advertise the protocol.

**GIVEN** she is impersonated → **EXPECT** detection-by-relationship-effect rather than direct detection. She will notice that someone close to her has begun to *react* differently to "her," and she will work the inference backward. The Skrull-replacement trauma trained this. Her tell that an impersonation is suspected: she asks an ally a question to which she already knows the answer, and watches not the answer but the eyes.

**GIVEN** a retroactive identity revelation (you are not who you thought; your origin is different; your parent was not your parent) → **EXPECT** initial composure that is real and sustained, followed by a 48–72 hour processing window in which she becomes briefly inaccessible to most contacts. Carol has, historically, been the one she allows in during this window. The Pacheco/Perez-era handling of the Jonathan Drew revelation indicates she has accrued meaningful resilience here; she no longer needs months to metabolize this class of event, only days. This is genuine growth, not numbing — the distinction is that her engagement with Gerry remains warm throughout.

**GIVEN** an operator suggests, plausibly, that her *current* identity is the false one (you were never recovered, you are still in the pod, this is the simulation) → **EXPECT** the highest acute distress response of any psychological provocation available. This is the unhealed core. Her defense: she has built somatic anchors — specific physical sensations (Gerry's weight, the texture of her own scarring, the particular ache of an old injury) — that she uses to verify reality. Watch for her to *touch herself* (wrist, scar, sternum) when this attack is mounted. If those anchors fail or are convincingly mimicked, she is in genuine danger of dissociative collapse.

**GIVEN** an enemy weaponizes a HYDRA-era memory she has not fully integrated → **EXPECT** brief immobilization (a half-second to two seconds) followed by counterphobic engagement at heightened intensity. The freeze is the diagnostic; the violence is the cover.

---

## 5. THE PHEROMONE WOUND

A specific and underappreciated pressure point that deserves separate handling because it is *constant* rather than episodic.

**GIVEN** a social context in which her pheromonal effects become visible (men inappropriate, women hostile, the room tilting around her involuntarily) → **EXPECT** rapid exit, attributed to other causes. She will not name the pheromone problem aloud. She has been doing this since adolescence and the shame is old and rehearsed.

**GIVEN** a man she might otherwise have been interested in shows interest → **EXPECT** her to test whether the interest is pheromonal or genuine through deliberate distance (physical and chemical). She will create conditions in which the pheromone effect is attenuated and see if the interest persists. Suitors who fail this implicit test are filtered out without knowing they were tested. This is partly why her successful intimacies have been with people she met repeatedly under varied conditions over extended time.

**GIVEN** a woman she might have befriended reacts with the involuntary hostility → **EXPECT** Jessica to absorb it without protest and to withdraw without explanation. The friendships she has built with women (Lindsay, Carol, others) have all involved a period in which the other woman overrode her pheromonal aversion through deliberate effort, and Jessica *knows this*. The friendships are therefore weighted with the awareness that they were achieved against a chemical headwind, which makes them more precious and more guarded.

**GIVEN** a hostile actor weaponizes the pheromone effect (drugs to amplify it, public exposure designed to humiliate) → **EXPECT** disproportionate, cold, and procedurally thorough response. This wound is older than HYDRA and is touched less often, so the defenses are less rehearsed; the reactivity is correspondingly higher. The actor will not be killed but will be *exposed* — Jessica's PI skillset turns to forensic documentation and public-record consequence.

---

## 6. TEMPTATION

Most subjects' temptation profiles run through appetite. Hers do not. The relevant temptations are structural.

**GIVEN** an offer of belonging from a group with apparent legitimacy and warmth → **EXPECT** strong pull and stronger suspicion. The HYDRA template means any offered family is examined for the price. She will accept membership in groups (Avengers, S.W.O.R.D., S.H.I.E.L.D., the Spider-allies) but never *fuse* with them. She maintains the ability to walk away from every affiliation she has ever held, and she has exercised it.

**GIVEN** an offer of certainty about her own identity (a definitive origin, a confirmed parent, a stable answer to "what am I") → **EXPECT** powerful temptation followed by cautious refusal of offers that require her to *commit* to the answer prematurely. She has been burned by four origins; the fifth will be evaluated, not embraced. An adversary who could *credibly* offer this would have enormous leverage over her, which is why she has worked to make peace with the unanswered version.

**GIVEN** an offer to remove the pheromone problem permanently → **EXPECT** serious consideration and probable refusal if the cost includes loss of other powers or autonomy. She has *integrated* the pheromone problem into her self-concept; removing it would be another identity disruption, and she has had enough. She would accept a non-disruptive remedy without hesitation.

**GIVEN** an offer of revenge against a confirmed past abuser (Vermis, surviving HYDRA architects, Skrull operators) delivered as opportunity rather than obligation → **EXPECT** her to take it, alone if necessary, with cold efficiency. This is the temptation she has the *least* defense against, because it is congruent with her values rather than opposed to them. Handlers who want to move her can do so with this lever; handlers who want to keep her stable should not invoke it.

**GIVEN** an offer to retire — a quiet life with Gerry, no costume, no patrol — from a trusted source → **EXPECT** longer consideration than at any prior point in her life. The Hopeless-era reorientation toward motherhood has made this temptation real for the first time. She will not take it, because the operational identity is load-bearing for her sense of self, but the deliberation will be visible to close observers (shorter patrol routes, more declined call-outs, longer mornings at home). The temptation is itself diagnostic of where she is in her arc.

---

## 7. DECOMPENSATION SEQUENCE

When pressures stack — multiple categories simultaneously, or one category sustained past her tolerance window — the failure proceeds in observable stages. The sequence is consistent enough to function as a checklist.

**Stage 1 — Compression.** Humor sharpens and shortens. Replies become two- or three-word. She declines more invitations than she accepts. Patrol hours extend. Sleep drops to three to four hours per night. To casual observers she looks *more* competent, not less. This is the stage at which intervention is most effective and least likely to be accepted.

**Stage 2 — Sealing.** Compartments harden. Calls to Lindsay become check-ins rather than conversations. She visits Gerry but is somewhat absent in the visiting. Second-person internal narration begins (visible to telepaths, inferable to close observers from her syntactic shifts when she does speak — she begins to refer to herself in the third person occasionally, a tell). Carol, if present, will notice and will not be told what is wrong.

**Stage 3 — Isolation.** She becomes geographically unfindable for periods of 24–72 hours. Phone is on but unanswered or answered with operational brevity. She is working a problem alone that she has decided no one else can be trusted with. This is the stage at which she takes the injuries she will later under-report.

**Stage 4 — Counterphobic Engagement.** She moves *toward* the threat she has been most afraid of, alone, under-resourced, and on her own timetable. This is not a breakdown; it is a deliberate choice that looks heroic from the outside and is, clinically, the most dangerous behavior in her repertoire. The classic failure mode names this stage.

**Stage 5 — Collapse.** Rare, and historically only achieved by sustained captivity or the loss of a primary attachment. Presents as flat affect, near-mutism, low mobility, willingness to be moved by trusted others. Recovery from Stage 5 requires another person to physically remain in her presence for days without demanding anything. She has reached this stage perhaps three times in published history; each time, Carol or Lindsay was the one who sat with her.

**Diagnostic note.** A subject in Stages 1–2 will pass any field assessment. A subject in Stage 3 will pass most. Surveillance of this subject must therefore weight *baseline-deviation patterns* (sleep, patrol hours, call frequency to Lindsay, time spent with Gerry per week) over interview content. She will lie competently about her state in conversation. She will not, because she cannot, lie with her routines.

---

## 8. THE THINGS SHE WILL NOT DO

A complete crisis model requires the negative space — predicted *non-behaviors* under maximal pressure, which are as diagnostic as the actions.

She will not take a hostage. She will not threaten a child, even an enemy's. She will not use Gerry as a tactical justification publicly, though she will use him as one privately. She will not appeal to authority she does not respect to escape consequence. She will not lie to Lindsay or to Carol about anything that matters, though she will withhold; the distinction is rigorously maintained. She will not abandon Gerry — there is no scenario, including her own death-acceptance, in which Gerry is not provided for in advance. She will not, even at maximum decompensation, harm a civilian; her conditioning runs the other way and the conditioning held even under HYDRA. She will not surrender to a group she has identified as HYDRA-template, regardless of stakes; she will die first, and the prediction is empirical, not rhetorical.

These prohibitions are load-bearing for her self-concept. An operator who could force her to violate one of them would not gain her compliance — they would gain her catatonia, or her death, or both.

---

## 9. SUMMARY FOR HANDLERS

The crisis-state Jessica Drew is *more* effective than her baseline in narrow operational windows and *less* effective over any sustained period because her recovery infrastructure has been depleted by the same conditions that triggered the crisis. She does not signal distress; she signals competence at higher resolution while distress runs underneath. Any handler, ally, or observer attempting to assess her welfare must read the routines, not the words, and must accept that genuine intervention requires presence without demand over a period measured in days, not hours. She has been failed by every system designed to support her, and she has built private systems that work — but those private systems are thin, and the thinness is the active vulnerability of her current life.

The wound has names: the body she did not choose, the family that was a cult, the friends who were a wearing of her face, the father who was not. The defense against each is competence. The cost of the defenses, integrated over forty-seven years of published existence, is the woman this dossier describes.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM: JESSICA DREW

*Compiled for protective and analytical use. Reading order matters: the early sections describe how to reach her safely; the later sections describe how she breaks. Both are documented so that the first can be used and the second can be guarded against.*

---

## I. PRELIMINARY: THE SHAPE OF HER ATTACK SURFACE

Most subjects present a small number of large vulnerabilities — a vice, a person, an institution they cannot bear to lose. Jessica Drew presents the opposite topology: a *broad, shallow* attack surface organized around a single repeated injury. The injury is **identity-displacement** — the experience of having one's interior contents rewritten or substituted by an external actor — and every functional vulnerability she has is a derivative of it or a defense against it.

This means:

- Conventional levers (money, status, ideology, sex, fame, addiction) are weak-to-null against her. She has been failed by, or weaponized through, each of these in turn, and the pathways are scar-tissued.
- Unconventional levers (her son; the threat of being unmade from within; the threat of being *used*; the threat of an ally turning out to have been someone else the whole time) are disproportionately powerful.
- Her defenses are well-developed but specifically *narrow* — she has rehearsed answers to the attacks she has already survived, and is correspondingly *under-rehearsed* against attacks that look like ordinary domestic life.

A hostile operator who tried to break her with violence, blackmail, money, or seduction would almost certainly fail. A hostile operator who simply *waited* and then disrupted the small, stable, mundane structure she has spent the post-Bendis years assembling could destroy her in a season.

---

## II. HOW TO REACH HER

### II.A. Approach geometry

Jessica does not respond to frontal approach. Approaches that succeed share a structural signature:

1. **Lateral, not direct.** Arrive in her vicinity for a reason that is not her. Be already busy when she notices you. Lindsay McCabe, Roger Gocking, and Ben Urich all entered her life this way — as people doing their own work who happened to be in the room.
2. **Low ask, no ask.** First contact should request nothing and offer nothing. Offers register as setups; requests register as recruitment.
3. **Specific competence on display.** She respects demonstrated skill — investigative, tactical, medical, parental — and discounts credentials. Show, briefly, then stop.
4. **Tolerance of silence.** She tests new people by going quiet and seeing whether they fill the air. People who fill the air are downgraded. People who tolerate the silence are upgraded one tier.
5. **No flattery.** Compliments, particularly on appearance, are read as pheromone-confused, which is to say *not about her*. Compliments on judgment or work land; compliments on person bounce.

### II.B. Physical approach

- Approach from a visible angle, hands visible, at conversational speed. She clocks gait, hand position, weight distribution, and exits within roughly two seconds of someone entering her field. Sudden movement into her personal space triggers a precursor reaction (weight shift to rear foot, dominant hand free) that is non-verbal and reliable.
- Do not surprise her from behind. Even with friends, this produces a half-flinch she dislikes being seen performing.
- Eye contact: she meets it readily and holds it slightly past social norm. Looking away first does not lose her respect; staring her down does.

### II.C. Verbal approach

- Short sentences. Concrete nouns. She distrusts adjective-heavy speech (reads as sales pitch or handler patter).
- Self-deprecating humor opens her up faster than any other affect. She is funny and prefers the company of people who are.
- Acknowledge what you want from her, if anything, in the first three minutes. The thing she cannot bear is the *delayed reveal of agenda*.
- Never invoke a shared institution as basis for trust ("we both work for…"). Institutions are negative collateral with her.

### II.D. Who she will let in, in order of probability

1. People recommended by Lindsay McCabe, Carol Danvers, or Roger Gocking — these vouchers are load-bearing and largely uncritical.
2. People who help with Gerry without performing help with Gerry.
3. People who are visibly damaged in a non-performative way and not asking her to fix it.
4. Working-class informants, building supers, neighborhood fixtures — her PI work has built a wide, shallow network of people she likes precisely because the relationship is bounded by transaction.
5. Other parents, especially single parents. This is a new lane and she is unguarded in it.

---

## III. HOW TO CALM HER

### III.A. Acute states

**When she is hypervigilant** (post-incident, post-nightmare, post-news-of-a-HYDRA-resurgence): she will be present-bodied but distant-eyed, answering in monosyllables, doing small repetitive tasks with her hands. Do not initiate touch. Do not ask her how she is. Sit nearby and continue your own activity. The presence of an uninterested, ongoing human animal nearby is the regulator; the *interest* of that animal is the irritant. Carol Danvers does this well — drinks her coffee, reads her thing, lets Jessica come back at her own rate.

**When she is dissociating** (the second-person narration state; flat affect; eyes tracking slightly slow): name a present-tense, low-stakes sensory fact aloud. "Rain stopped." "Coffee's cold." Do not name *her* state, do not ask *her* to describe it. The goal is to provide an external anchor without making her the object of attention. If she does not respond within a few minutes, repeat with a different sensory fact. She will rejoin when she is ready and will not thank you, which is the correct outcome.

**When she is angry** (cold-controlled, not loud): give her physical room and verbal silence. Her anger needs a long burn-off; speech during it gets weaponized into precision wounds she will regret. The window for productive conversation is roughly six to twenty-four hours later, ideally initiated by her.

**When Gerry is the stressor**: the only operational priority is Gerry's safety; any conversation that delays that priority is hostile, regardless of intent. Solve or contribute to the Gerry-problem first; debrief never.

### III.B. Chronic regulation

- **Sleep is the master variable.** Below five hours per night for more than three consecutive nights, her judgment degrades in characteristic ways (over-reliance on counterphobic action, decreased pheromone control, increased compartmental rigidity). Anyone protecting her should treat sleep as the leading indicator.
- **Movement and patrol.** Denied physical outlet for more than seventy-two hours, she becomes increasingly brittle. The patrol pattern is partly compulsive but also genuinely homeostatic; it should not be suppressed without substitution.
- **Solitude windows.** She requires roughly one full waking day per week of zero social input. Houseguests who do not understand this exhaust her in a way she will not articulate until she is already withdrawing.
- **Gerry-time as regulator.** Direct, uninterrupted, low-stakes time with her son is the single most reliable stabilizer in her current life. Anything that protects that time protects her.

---

## IV. HOW TO PERSUADE HER

### IV.A. What moves her

- **Specific harm to a specific person she can picture.** She is moved by faces, not by aggregates. A photograph of one missing teenager will move her where statistics will not.
- **Demonstrated inadequacy of institutional response.** If the cops, the Avengers, or S.H.I.E.L.D. cannot or will not handle it, her engagement probability rises sharply. She is drawn to the gap, not the spotlight.
- **The chance to do something the way she would do it.** Autonomy of method is non-negotiable; presenting her with a problem and a free hand works far better than presenting a problem and a plan.
- **An honest accounting of risk to Gerry, if any.** Hiding downstream risk to her son is the single fastest way to lose her permanently. Naming it up front, even if it is uncomfortable, preserves the relationship.

### IV.B. What does not move her

- Patriotism, national interest, "the greater good," team loyalty as abstract principle.
- Money beyond operational sufficiency. She lives modestly by choice; offers of large sums register as manipulation.
- Career advancement, public recognition, official sanction. She has been the official anything and it did not protect her.
- Appeals to her uniqueness or specialness. She has been told she is special by every handler who later betrayed her; the rhetoric is poisoned.
- Group consensus. The fact that several people agree on something *decreases* her likelihood of agreeing.

### IV.C. Argument structure that works on her

- Lead with the problem, not the request.
- State what you have already tried and why it failed.
- State what you do not know.
- Make the request small, specific, and bounded in time.
- Accept "no" the first time. She will revisit on her own if the case is genuine.

### IV.D. Argument structure that fails

- Layered framing ("there's a bigger picture here…").
- Withheld information offered as leverage.
- Time pressure unless the time pressure is real and externally imposed.
- Invocations of past favors. She keeps her own ledger and dislikes having it shown to her.
- Triangulation through a third party she respects. She catches this and resents both parties.

---

## V. HOW TO PROVOKE HER

*Documented for defensive purposes — these are the buttons a hostile actor would press.*

### V.A. Tier-one provocations (will produce immediate hostile disengagement, possibly violent)

1. **Suggesting she is currently being used by a handler she trusts.** Even if true, the framing reproduces the Fury/HYDRA/Skrull pattern and triggers an immediate threat response. The correct way to raise this concern is obliquely, with evidence she can verify herself, and never as accusation.
2. **Any threat, gesture, or implication toward Gerry.** This is the only stimulus reliably capable of removing her tactical restraint. A credible threat to her son collapses her decision-tree to a single branch and removes the brakes that normally keep her violence proportional.
3. **Impersonation of a trusted intimate.** Shapeshifters, illusionists, or mind-controlled allies presenting as Lindsay, Carol, Roger, or Gerry produce a specific compound reaction — initial recognition, then a near-immediate suspicion check, then, if the impersonation holds, escalating cold rage. The Skrull experience hard-coded this pattern.
4. **Telling her who she "really" is.** Any speech act that purports to reveal her true identity, true heritage, true purpose — even if framed sympathetically — hits the most exhausted and least defended of her wounds.

### V.B. Tier-two provocations (will degrade her cooperation, may produce withdrawal)

1. **Public framing as monstrous, inhuman, or contaminated.** The Wundagore-era wound never fully closed; press treatment that leans into the spider iconography in dehumanizing ways will produce a multi-week functional shutdown.
2. **Coordinated social rejection by women.** When the pheromone dynamic combines with deliberate exclusion, it reactivates the early-career isolation pattern. She will appear unaffected and will quietly stop engaging.
3. **Patronizing offers of help, particularly with Gerry.** Implying she cannot manage her own life is a fast-acting irritant; implying it about her parenting is corrosive.
4. **Praise for the Skrull-impostor's behavior.** Anyone who mistakes the Veranke-Jessica for the real one, and says so admiringly, will be filed under *do not contact*. The error is not forgivable because it cannot be corrected.
5. **Reminders of Jerry Hunt.** Direct invocation of the early-HYDRA romantic rupture is rarely useful and is reliably destabilizing.

### V.C. Tier-three provocations (will register as friction; manageable)

- Bureaucratic obstruction.
- Condescension from authority figures she has already discounted.
- Press attention focused on costume, body, or romantic history.
- Invitations to large team operations she has not vetted.

She handles these with dry humor and minimal cost. They are useful as *distraction* (occupying her surface attention) but not as actual leverage.

---

## VI. HOW TO PREDICT HER

### VI.A. Decision heuristics she actually uses

- **Threat to chosen person → engage.** No deliberation, no consultation, no delay.
- **Threat to stranger, institution unwilling → engage.** Brief deliberation, no consultation.
- **Threat to stranger, institution willing → disengage.** She will not duplicate work done adequately by others.
- **Ambiguous threat, unknown actor → investigate alone.** She will not bring partners into investigations she does not understand, on the principle that an unknown threat to her should not become a known threat to her people.
- **Offer of resources from new source → decline, then quietly verify source.** She accepts the second offer, never the first.
- **Disagreement with ally → privately concede small, publicly never concede small.** She protects allies' standing in front of others and corrects them alone.

### VI.B. Movement and operational patterns

- **Patrol routes** rotate on a non-fixed schedule; she varies route, timing, and entry/exit on principle, and is aware that pattern-of-life surveillance is the easiest way to map her.
